all things; they would not observe Gods Law and Covenant without addition or
diminution, they would follow their own inventions: Therefore says the Lord,
they should serve their Enemies in hunger, cold, and nakedness, in the want of
all things, and in a strange Land.

Consider (dearly beloved) That from the excellency of Government does arise
the happiness and blessedness of the Saints in the Kingdom of Heaven: I pray
you therefore let us set a high price upon Government. Let us proceed warily in
matter of Government; let us enquire of God, let us follow the purest, the most
clear and evident presidents and prescriptions, without turning to the right or
left hand; let us enquire for the old and good ways, prescribed, owned, and
blessed by God himself; against this there can be no just exception: And it may
be God will see and regard us, and remember the riches of his own compassion,
of his own precious promises, Isai. 1.26. God will restore (which argues they
then were not in being) Judges as at the first, and Counselors as at the
beginning, then shall we be called a City of Righteousness, a faithful City.

I might multiply Testimonies, the Scripture is obvious and copious, but time
bids me forbear; Therefore I go on to consider a little more particularly
Kings, concerning whom the most high and wise God did both see and know what
and when the first King should be, and how long the continuance of the
Government of Kings should continue, and when their Kingdoms should be
finished; of this I doubt not, now the end of Kings and all other afflictions
work together for the glory of God, and the good of Gods Elect: and I doubt not
but that God would use some Kings as instruments, in some particulars, to be
helpful to his Church and People.

Object. Some (and too many) use this as an argument, That Kings were good for
Gods Church and People; for, say they, did not God make Promises to Kings of
good things? and were not some Kings good instruments in some things to promote
Gods glory? Did not Solomon build a Temple to the name of the Lord? etc.

Ans. One instance consider, Adam our great Grandfather, after he had broken
Gods Commandment, and eaten the forbidden fruit, after this, and presently upon
the occasion of what came to pass by reason of his transgression, God out of
his bounty and goodness makes a Promise of great worth to Adam and to his
posterity, namely, That the seed of the woman should breaks the serpents head:
Consider now, would it be safe or sound arguing to argue thus? Adam did well,
because God in mercy gave him a precious promise? No verily; Or would it be
safe to say, That we, some of his posterity, may follow his steps in sinning,
because that he obtained a precious promise? No verily; because we are first to
have respect to Gods Covenant, to his Law; And also we are to consider, That
the root from whence this promise sprung, was not from, or because God was
pleased with (or approved of) Adams transgression; but the Promise sprung out
of Gods abundant and rich mercy, and free grace.

From the premised respects and considerations I gather and conclude, That
those gracious promises, or acts, wherein God used Kings as instruments or
actors in some good things, these do neither approve of the Government by
Kings, nor do they prove that the institution of Kings was approved by God; and
much less do they prove, That the Government by Kings was of equal goodness
with the Government by Judges; in which the Word of God is plain and evident,
That God prescribed, owned, and blessed the Government by Judges: And
contrarily the Word of God is plain, evident, and copious, That God did not
allow of the Government by Kings, but did expressly disapprove of that form of
Government by Kings; and to this we may add the experience of the fruits of
Kings to this very day.

Object. Some do use this argument to strengthen the continuance of Kings,
namely, That God did foretell that Kings should be, and some Kings God did
himself appoint.

Ans. God did foretell that Israel would kick with their feet, and slight his
Commandments; God did foretell that the people would reap bitter fruits from
Kings: This does not show, that God did allow or approve either of the one, or
of the other.

God did appoint some Kings immediately, showing, that in this way, if the
people had kept close to God, and have gone no further backward from his Rules
and Directions, then it should have been better and safer for the People; it
was too much to alter the form prescribed by God, but it was an addition to
and aggravation of this sin, when they slighted God and did not enquire of
God, who should be the man that should be their King, from time to time. When
they followed the Rule and made him King whom the Lord did choose, (it may be
noted that) God chose Saul immediately by lot, wherein we may note that although
God were angry, yet he took thus much care for the People, that God let Saul
(rightfully) reign no longer as King, but so long as he walked in Gods ways,
and during that time God gave Saul some portion of his good Spirit, or a spirit
which made him suitable in some proportion to govern his People, as appears. 1 Samuel 10.9. God gave Saul another hearts, and all those tokens came to pass,
etc. And when Saul departed from God, and forsook his Law, we may note that
God rejected him from being King. 1 Samuel 15. ver. 26. Thou have cast away the
word of the Lord, and the Lord has cast away thee that thou shall not be King
over Jsrael. Ver. 28. Then Samul said unto him, the Lord has rent the Kingdom
of Israel, from thee this day. And note now, that when Saul was deposed, Chap.
16.14. The Spirit of the Lord departed from Saul, and an evil spirit sent of
the Lord vexed him.

We may note, that because the people made David King a man chosen by God,
(and not by the peoples rash proceedings) that God gave to David his good and
blessed Spirit. 1 Samuel 16.13. Then Samuel took an horn of Oil and anointed
him (David) in the midst of his Brethren: and the spirit of the Lord came
upon David from that day forward: here we may note that it is no vain thing
that God should appoint our governors for us, God let the people taste of the
difference between Kings and Judges, in that Solomon set up or countenanced
Idolatry, and laid great taxations upon the people, yet it did not extend so
far, not by very much, as afterward the People felt under the government of
other Kings, which were set up rashly by the people, without such an immediate
call, (and for ought I know) not being anointed with Oil, by any true Prophet
of God.

This I note the rather, because I have respect to God his express Command and
Direction (which was never reversed to this very Day) recorded, Deuteronomy. 17.14.
where God says if thou shall say, I will set a King over me like as all the
Nations that are about me. Ver. 25. Tou shall make him King over thee, whom
the Lord thy God shall choose.

I shall only at the present observe these two notes from this place, first
that God does not hereby either command, or allow that the People should set up
a Government by Kings; for the Lord says, if thou shall say I will set a King
over me, this came to pass in the Days of Samuel. Then the people they would
have a King, the People here did not inquire of God, first now it does not
follow, that because the People said we will have a King, that therefore God
does either approve or allow of this matter, but the direct contrary appears,
1 Samuel 8. in most eminent manner.

But secondly, I do observe that God says thou shall (if thou will be wilful
and have a King, yet) thou shall make him King whom the Lord thy God shall
choose; here I put a real difference between a King or governor being chosen by
God immediately, and between the choice that the People make, I purpose if God
will to speak more of this in place afterward.

But this Rule also the People soon forsook, namely they made themselves
Kings of their own choosing, wherein ( I conceive) they did not inquire of God,
who should be the man, therefore the Lord says they had Princes and he knew
it not; that is to say, they did not according to the Rule inquire of God, who
should be King. Thus much to show, that it was better with the People when they
eyed God, and kept close to the Rule (when God chose the person) then it was
when they fell more foully as afterward they did; but this still does not prove
that God did institute that form of government by Kings, or much less that
this form of government was as good, and as well approved of by God, or so
blessed, as the government by Judges.

But to go on to speak more punctually, or more particularly to the being of
Kings; I shall endeavor (according to the measure of grace received) to speak
of them in true proportion, as God has spoken of them in the holy and sacred
Scriptures.

The first King that I find recorded was Abimeleck, Judges 9. it is noted that
this Man was no lawful governor appointed by God; but one that usurped the
Kingdom, because he entered not by and according to the true way, wherein and
whereby, God had prescribed; which I believe was principally in regard that the
People did not enquire of God, who should govern them: but contrarily the
People chose him out of, or for sinister respect, because of affinity, kindred,
and also, because he entered by force; we may see what is recorded Judges. 9.
By this man's government there were very sad events, or fruits that followed or
sprung, for he was the occasion of much evil and bloodshed; this serves to
warn us to take heed that we enquire of God who shall govern us, and that we
do follow the most clear and evident Rules and Presidents, prescribed and
recorded in the sacred Scriptures the sure Rules of Truth: our Savior teaches
that the true Shepherd enters at the true door, that is, according to the
revealed will of God. And on the contrary those Wolves and Foxes, do enter in
at the window, that is (as I conceive) by some way that God has not
prescribed, as by friends out of by respects, or by Fraud, Force, Money,
Beauty, Personage, Eloquence, or such like; all of them not in such away as is
prescribed in the most unerring Rules of Truth.

After him arose Saul to be King, concerning his person, he was truly and
rightfully called, being chosen by God, but concerning the form of government
by Kings; this was the Peoples invention, in imitation of the Heathen Nations,
as appears, 1 Samuel 8.5. The people said make us a King to judge us like all
Nations: from this place I observe that it was not the Peoples demand to have
this, or that man in particular to be their King; but they desire only to have
a King. By which it appears that this sin lay, not in regard of the person,
but it was in respect to the form of government; before they were governed by
Judges, which Form of govermnent God did immediately prescribe and own it,
and bless it; but this Form of government by Kings the people they did invent
it, in imitation of the Nations round about; concerning those Nations God had
expressly said, that they should not follow the manners and customs of the
Nations.

But secondly, against this way of government by Kings God does (I believe)
expressly, evidently, and eminently oppose himself, in these particulars:

First God says, that (by this means or way that the people here lusted
after) they had cast off God from being their King, or reigning over them.
Which is expressed, 1 Samuel 8.7. They have not cast thee away, but they have
cast me away, that I should not reign over them; this ( I conceive) is
plainly implied, and expressed, that the greatness of their sin lay in
regard of the form, and not in regard of the person, as if God should have
said, they have not so much sinned in desiring another Governor, (although I
believe this also was their sin) but they now have rejected the form of
government by me immediately prescribed.

Further God opposes this form of Government by Kings, immediately in showing
the People the great evils that they should reap, by Kings, noted, 1 Samuel 8.
From Ver. 9. to Ver. 19. Kings will take your Sons, and your Daughters from
you, and will appoint them to serve themselves. (This God does not say was
lawful for Kings to do) for Gods Law was express to the contrary, Exodus
22.21. Moreover thou shall not do injury to a stranger. Neither did Gods Laws
permit that they should wrong any man: and Samuel uses that as a strong
argument to convince them of their evil, namely, in these words, 1 Samuel 12.3.
Behold here J am, bear record before the Lord of me, whose Ox have I taken,
or whose Ass have I taken, or whom have I done wrong unto, or whom have I
hurt? Ver. 4. Then the People said thou have done us no wrong, nor have hurt
us, neither have thou taken any thing of any Man's hand. Hereby appears the
Peoples great evil and ingratitude, and their unrighteousness in forsaking
that government, with which they could find no fault. Further this showed that
Kings would prove great evils, because they would be great wrongers, and great
oppressors, because they would take by violence their choicest comforts from
the People. And further this showed, that Kings would rule by the Rules of
their own wills, (in our days called their prerogatives) this is showed in
these expressions, Kings will take these and these things from you, but this
they ought not to do, for herein Samuel shows his integrity: we may observe
that the Law of God ought to be the guide, the Rule, and the bounds, to all men
high and low, to King and People, this is evident, Deuteronomy. 17.16. to 20. There
God says, that the King should have the Book of the Law, and that he should
read therein all the days of his life, that he may learn to fear the Lord
his God: and to keep all the words of this Law, and these Ordinances to do
them: that his heart be not lifted up above his Brethren, and that he turn
not to the right hand, or to the left hand, etc. From hence we may see that the
King is not to do what he lists: but he is as expressly commanded to observe
and do the Law, as any other man, yea and in some sort more, because his
example is more prevalent to draw others, either to good or evil.

But further we may here note the difference between Kings and Judges; the
Kings they will do thus and thus, they will break the bounds set unto them,
but the Judges were humble meek men, this God knew when he put in that clause
(so nearely linked to the observation of his Law) namely, that his heart be not
lifted up above his Brethren; experience has taught us much of this (could we
be warned) That Kings their hearts will be lifted up. Observe I pray you, the
Judges they acknowledged the People to be their Brethren, but Kings they say
their blood and their descent is more Royal, more Illustruous, more Excellent,
then those they call the baser sort, and the more ignoble.

It is to be noted that in the first and purest times, those men that were
truly godly, truly virtuous, those men that were most precize, that were the
most observant of the Law of God. Those men then were accounted to be the most
noble, and so we find they were in Gods esteem (for we find Moses taken
from keeping the sheep. And Gideon from threshing, and David from the
Sheepe-fold, and made Rulers of the People. But the World is now turned
upside-downe, for what do some men now applaud and worship but the Blood
Royal, and Noble Blood? we have men now, that are truly noble and eminent for
Piety, that sway the government of the Commonwealth; but what is the tumult?
They say they cannot see their Nobility. (I would speak soberly and
forbearingly,) consider warily and truly, is it not because the God of this
World has blinded the eyes of many men?

But let us further note that this King Saul, or a King, or the Government by
Kings, would not only deprive the People of their Sons and Daughters, but
also Kings would take their seed and their Vinyards, 1 Samuel 8.15. Their
Menservants and their Maide-servants, and the chief of your young men, and
your Asses, and Sheep: and ye shall be his servants; Note I pray you, that
this People had great liberty and freedom under the government by Judges
(could they have improved these with thankful and contented hearts) but they
would reject and slight these mercies, they would be governed by Kings, under
which Government they should endure many afflictions, but when it comes to
this height, that they themselves should be servants, then they begin to be
more sensible, then they cry out, but says God, Ver. 18. The Lord will not
hear you in the day, and time of these afflictions.

By this evident admonition it plainly appeared that God opposed in threatening
manner, this government by Kings, for note that the cause here was not so much
about the person to be made King, but it was about the form of government by
Kings. Note further how Samuel humbly and patiently does argue the cause with
the People Chap. 12. ver. 7. to 13. where Samuel puts the People in mind
how God had not bin wanting to them, but from time to time had raised up and
appointed good governors for them. Which governors God protected, guided and
blessed to them, and made them Saviors (and not oppressors nor destroyers) to
them; sometimes (for their sins, and to prove them whether they would cleave
to God, and to show them the benefit that it was to have God to appoint good
governors, and for other ends which God knew to be for his glory and their
good) God did leave them without chief Judges, and then we see the People they
run into many bypath, and sinful courses, and then God suffered them to
feel afflictions by enemies; but note that when the people considered the
cause and sought the favor of God, and cried to God to help them, God never
failed but answers their petitions; note in what manner God answered them, he
raised up Judges, which God made to be blessings, and Saviors to the People.

From this expostulation of Samuel, we may observe that God by Samuel reproves
the People for altering that form of government which God in his wisdom had
prescribed, and blessed to the People; And the People could not deny the truth
of this: but further note that God to the end that posterity to come might
evidently see his displeasure, for that cause, because the People had altered
the form of government by Judges, and instead thereof had wilfully and
obstinately desired a government by Kings, Therefore the Lord shows the
People by an eminent and wonderful way expressed thus; 1 Samuel 12.17. I will
call unto the Lord and he shall send Thunder and Rain, that ye may perceive
and see how that your wickedness is great, which ye have done in the sight of
the Lord, in asking you a King. Ver. 18. Then Samuel called unto the Lord, and
the Lord sent Thunder and Rain the same Day, and all the People feared the
Lord, and Samuel exceedingly. Ver. 19. The People said we have sinned in
asking us a King besides all our other sins, etc.

Concerning this King we have occasion to note, that Gods Presence did remove
now and stand at a further distance then before, God did not wholly depart from
them, but remembering the multitude of his mercies, he did still favor the
People, but as the Tabernacle, for the sins of the People was removed out of
the Host, Exodus 33.7.8. (Yet not wholly out of their sight) so here God removed
his gracious presence further off from the People.

The next King was David, who was a good and virtuous King, God would not
afflict the People so much that they should have no good Kings. David's
blemishes I forbear, though some blemishes he had, such as (I believe) were not
to be found amongst the Judges, that were immediately appointed by God to their
place after succeeded Solomon, how far he declined from the straight Rules of
Gods revealed Will, are to be found recorded in the Book of Kings.

Rehoboam Reigned, he had 18. Wives and threescore Concubines, and desired many
Wives, 2 Cro 11, 21 23. He forsook the Law of the Lord, and all Israel with
him, for which cause Shishack came up against Jerusalem, and took the strong
Cities, which were of Judah: The People were made servants to Shishack. 2 Cro.
12.1. to 9. Further he did evil and prepared not his heart to seek the Lord.
Ver. 14. Ahijam reigns, he walked in all the sins which his Father had done
before him, and his heart was not perfect with the Lord, 1 King. 15.3. Asa
reigned he did that which was right in the eyes of the Lord, he put down his
Mother, because she had an Idol in a Grove. 1 King. 15. Nadab reigned, he did
evil in the sight of the Lord, and made Israel sin. 1 King. 15.26. Baashaw
reigns, he did evil in the sight of the Lord, and caused Israel to sin. 1
King. 16. Elah he reigned, did evil, being drunk was slain. 1 King. 16. Omri
reigns he did evil in the sight of the Lord, worse then all that were before
him. 1 King. 16. Zimri reigns was burnt. 1 King. 16.18. Ahab the son of
Omri reigns and did worse then all before him. 1 King. 16.3. Ahaziah
reigns, he did evil, he sought help of Baallzebub, the God of Ecron. 2
King. 1. Iehoram reigns, he did evil in the sight of the Lord. 2 Kin. 3.2.
Iehosaphat reigns, he did that which was right in the eyes of the Lord. 2
Kings. Ioram reigns, he did evil. 2 Kin. 8.9. Jehoram son of Iehosaphat
reigns, he did evil. 2 Kin 8.17. Jehu reigns, he regarded not to walk in
the Law of the Lord God. 2 Ki. 10.31. He is an occasion to cause Israel to sin,
and therefore they are smitten in all the Coasts of Israel. Ver. 23. Athalia
reigns, did evil is slain. 2 Ki. 11.3.6. Iehoash reigns, he did good in
the Eyes of the Lord during the time the Priest taught him. 2 Ki. 12.2. But the
high places were not taken away, he is slain. Ver. 21. Iehoaash son of Iehu
reigns, did evil in the sight of the Lord, and causes Israel to be
delivered into the hands of their enemies. 2 Ki. 13.2.3. The Destruction of the
People was so great, that there was left but 50 Horsemen, and 10 Charrets, and
10000 Footmen, they were destroyed and made like Dust beaten to powder. 2 Ki.
13.6, 7. Iehoash son of Iehoaash reigns, he did evil in the sight of the
Lord. 2 Ki. 13.10.11. Jeroboam reigns, he did evil in the sight of the Lord.
2 Ki. 14.23, 24. Amaziah reigns, did uprightly in the Eyes of the Lord, but
not like David. 2 Ki. 14.3. Azariah reigns, did uprightly in the Eyes of the
Lord, but they burnt Incense in the high places, and the Lord smote the King,
and he was a Leper to the Day of his Death. 2 Ki. 15.3 4, 5. Zachariah
reigns, he did evil in the sight of the Lord, 2 Ki. 15.8.9. Shallum
reigns, is slain, 2 Ki. 15, 14. Menahem reigns, did evil, 2 Ki. 15.17,
18. Pekahiah reigns, He did evil in the sight of the Lord. 2 Ki. 15.23, 24.
Pekah reigns, He did evil. 2 Ki. 15.28. The People carried away captive.
Iotham reigns He did uprightly, but the People burnt incense in the high
places, in his Days, the Lord sent enemies upon the People. 2 Ki. 5.34, 37.
Ahab reigns, He consecrated his Son in the fire, he did much evil. 2 Ki.
16. Hoshea reigns, He did evil in the sight of the Lord, he becomes
servant to Salmanasser King of Ashur. 2 Ki. 17.2, 3. The People besieged, and
carried captive. Ver. 6. Because they kept not Gods commands diligently. 37.
Hezechiah reigns, He did uprightly, according to all that David. 2 Ki. 18.
Manasseh reigns, He did evil in the sight of the Lord, after the
abomination of the Heathen. 2 Ki. 21.2. He did much evil, and filled Jerusalem
from corner to corner with innocent blood, 2 Ki. 21.16. And he caused Judah to
sin, and to do evil. Ver. 16. Ammon reigns, He did much evil in the sight
of the Lord, 2 Ki. 21.20. Josiah He reigns, He did uprightly in the sight of
the Lord, 2 Ki. 22.2. Iehoahaz his Son reigns, he did much evil in Gods
sight. 2 Ki. 23.32. The Land in his Days was put under great tribute. Ver. 33.
Iehojachin reigns, He did evil. 2 Ki. 23.37. very much evil. Iehojachin his
Son, He reigns, He did much evil, 2 Ki. 24.9. The People carried captive
in his Days very much People, Ver. 13.4. Zedechiah He reigns, and He did
evil in the sight of the Lord, very much 2 Ki. 24.9 20.

It is well to be considered of, that amongst all the Judges of Israel, (that
came into their places according to Gods institution) there was not one man of
them (that I know of) that was taken away by the Sword of the enemy, nor by
treachery slain by their own People, nor came to any untimely Death (save one
man) and that was not for practical evil of himself, but for suffering sin
to go without due punishment, in his children. But contrarily they are noted
much for Humility, Sincerity, and Piety. Certainly, the Spirit of God does
wisely describe Governors, for our learning, had we but hearts wisely and
diligently to observe them. But note contrarily that amongst the Kings, how
many were taken away by untimely Deaths, some by Gods command slain, some by
the Sword of the enemy, some carried captive, and the greater part slain by
the People; and the most of them are noted to be notorious sinners. I shall
rehearse some of them, although I believe not all.

The first fruits of their King Abimelecke, Judge. 9.6.53. The next was Saul,
slain, was his own Executioner, 1 Samuel 31.4. Nadab slain by one of his own
people, 1 Ki. 15.27. Elah slain in like manner, 1 Ki. 16.9. And of Baasha his
predecessors progeny, God says. 1 Ki. 16.4. he that dies of Baasha his stock
in the City, him shall the Dogs eat, and he that dies in the field the
Fowls. After him Zimri pursued by the People, burns himself, 1 Ki. 16.18.
Jehoram slain by his own people. 2 Ki. 9. Ahaziah slain in like manner. 2 Ki.
9.27. Iesabell slain, 2 Ki. 9. Ahab slain, his posterity slain, 2 Ki. 10.6.
by the Elders of his own people. Ver. 7. Athalia slain by her own people. 2
Ki. 11.3.16. Iehoash slain by his own servants. 2 Ki. 12.20. Shallum slain by
his own people. 2 Ki. 15.10.12. Pekahiah slain by his own people. 2 Ki. 15 25.
Pekah slain by his own people. 2 Ki. 15.30. Amon slain by his own people. 2
Ki. 21.23:

I know not any one of these, but that they are noted to be notorious sinners,
I do let pass some others slain, and carried captives, only these briefly
(as the shortness of time will permit) the Lord give us hearts to understand
the meaning of the blessed spirit of God aright. Note here that God in his
righteous Judgments suffered, and appointed Kings to be punished on earth. God
did not let them alone to be punished in another World.

I do believe that all these were not to be approved in the instruments and
manner of their slaughters; but some of them are approved, and all of them are
noted to be taken away by Gods righteous judgments, for the breach of his
Laws and Commandments.

Now let the sincere godly hearted unpartially compare this government by
Kings, with that government by judges, in which I pray God to direct you aright.

Thus have I endeavored to present to our view the Kings that reigned over
Judah and Israel, the Lord give us understanding to consider what bitter fruits
the People reaped by changing their form of Government. I shall only in this
matter consider that (doubtless) these Kings many of them or others in their
room would have been much better, had the People kept closer to the Rules
prescribed, and from time to time enquired of God, who should have been the
man that should have governed them; for we may note that although God promsed
David, that some of his posterity should govern; yet they ought to have made
him King whom the Lord should choose, Deuteronomy. 17. But we may note that God did so
withdraw his good Spirit from the people, that I remember not that it is
recorded from Solomon's time and after, that the People did ever solemnly
enquire counsel of God, Who should govern them. I do believe that if the
people had solemnly and seriously sought to God in this matter, God would have
provided some of David's posterity from time to time, and so have blessed and
guided them by his good Spirit, that they should have been much better then
they were; but I do believe God suffered them to swerve, that we by their
examples might learn wisdom, whatsoever was written before time was written
for our learning.

Having thus far proceeded in laying down, or describing the Cause or
Foundation, wherefore or whereupon I endeavor (in the fear and love of the
great and most high God according to the measure of Grace received) to describe
such a government, Governors, together with their entrances and authority, as
God has prescribed, owned and blessed; in all which I do consider, that from
the time of the Prophet Samuel to this day, there has been so great a
swerving and declining, from that first most pure, and clear Fountain, from
those most straight, wholesome, and good Rules, Precepts, and Commandments,
described by that most high and only Wise God; therefore I pray you blame me
not if I decline from humane authorities, in all this description, I desire to
enquire for the old and good ways of our good God. And I consider that Gods
Ways, (his good Will and Pleasure,) is most certainly (most wisely, most
apparently) made known in the Scriptures written by the Prophets and Apostles,
men that most truly and faithfully made known Gods good Will and Pleasure
(without mixture of their own or other men's inventions.) Therefore I shall
most chiefly and only in comparison, allege the authority of the Scriptures:
and the rather because I consider that as the interposition of the Earth,
between the Sun and Moon, darkneth that light (and makes an Eclipse) whereby
we are hindered from the more apparent and clear light and benefit, that
otherwise we might receive; so I fear it would come to pass, if I should
follow other inventions; I am sure that in this way the true light is most
unerring. I shall next endeavor to show what encouragement I find recorded in
the sacred Scripture, that do strengthen or encourage me to believe; That God
now in these latter Days and Times, will restore and reform government, so
that we shall have Judges as at the first, and counselors as at the beginning:
and then we shall be called a City of righteousness a faithful City. I shall
begin to propound to consideration this Scripture, Esai. 1.24. Thus says the
Lord of Hosts, the mighty one of Israel, Ah I will ease me of mine adversaries,
and avenge me of mine en mies. Ver. 25. Then will I turn mine hand upon thee,
and burn out thy dross till it be pure, and take away all thy tin. Ver. 26.
And I will restore thy Judges as at the first, and thy counselors as at the
beginning, afterward thou shall be called a City of righteousness a faithful
City.

From this place I observe, That corrupt Governors are the great hindrances of
Reformation, because the Church shall then be a City of righteousness, when
they have Judges as at the first.

Secondly, I observe, That such corrupt Governors, and Governments God has
determined shall be put down, this is expressed in these words, J will ease me
of my enemies and burn out thy Dross, this is plainly employed in these
words, I will restore thy Judges as at the first, etc.

Thirdly, I observe that at this time when the Prophet Esaias wrote this sentence
or this precious promise. The government that then was in being (which was a
government by Kings) was neither the first government, nor the best, or pure
government; but hereby noted to be a corrupt government: If this were not the
plain and true meaning of these words (I believe) God would not have made this
to be the way and means, whereby the Church should become (in Gods estimation)
a City of righteousness, and a faithful City, and this appears if we do
consider that the way how, and cause why, they should become a City of
righteousness, was Because a better government should be to the Church and
People of God, and that which then was in being should be destroyed, but then
the government was by Kings.

Fourthly, I observe that this government should be reformed, or regulated
according to the first and purest times, and by Judges, which being considered
(I believe) it plainly follows that from the time of Samuel to this day this
prophecy has not bin fulfilled and accomplished; because, there has not from
that time to this bin such a Reformation, such a Government by Judges, as was
in the first and most pure times, instituted, the most immediately, by God
himself; and is held out in these words, As at the first, etc.

Fifthly, I observe that there is just ground to hope and believe that such a
Reformation God will work, namely, that God will restore Judges as at the
first.

Sixthly, I believe there are good grounds from this place (compared with the
acts and great works that, God is now working, and has wrought) to expect,
that this very time, is the time, or the beginning of the time God pointed out
in this prophecy; Because, that corrupt government by Kings is put down, in
such a way of burning and righteousness, as has not bin from that time to
this day (as I believe) and such an earnest seeking and strong endeavors, as
has not bin usual, for to set up and restore a government by Judges as at the
first; in which endeavors I cannot but acknowledge that (I believe) it
evidently appears. That, many men have affectionately endeavored (with the
hazard of their lives and of all their worldly comforts) to obtain a
government, such as might be for the glory of God and according to his Will
revealed, as at the first.

Object. How comes it then to pass that sin abounds so much, and that
wickedness is not more suppressed?

Answ. We are to consider that great works are not always finished, so soon
as they are begun. God may suffer some sins now more then ordinary to appear,
that by that means we may see them, and see the ev^ll of them, and the danger
of them, and by seeing them we may see how, and where they may be rooted up:
this government is yet in agitation not fully settled, (as I conceive) they
have many occasions, their Enemies not wholly subdued.

We may observe that in those times when God was about to work the greatest
deliverances for his Church, God works by contraries, (in man's apprehension,)
when Israel was nearest to their deliverance out of Aegyt, then God let them
taste the most bitterly of he yoke of their oppression, although Moses at the
same instant was laboring for their deliverance.

Secondly, can we see no reformation? consider, that the Gospel has free
liberty to be preached, many Congregations are much reformed, and a free
liberty for Reformation to others, Idolatry is suppressed, the Ministry and
People are freed from those troubles in conscience, that formerly they would
have been glad to have been eased of, and further consider, that in these
times there is much more light; many things (formerly obscured and hid) are now
appeared, and concerning those sins that are a just cause of grief (I believe
when government is settled) they will be driven away as chafe before the wind;
and touching those Burdens and Taxations, I believe they are our governors
grief to impose them, and I hope God will show them a means to ease them, and
to take them away; in the mean time let us seek God unfainedly, and God will
answer us graciously.

Thirdly, let us consider which party (those that are for, or those that are
against this present government or Army) be most guilty of the sin, most
reigning; I shall speak something what my own experience reaches, and so far
as my memory and opportunity has received from other men.

Those generally that stand for the Army and Parliament are godly, or civil
the most of them, I know not one other ways.

Those that are against them are many of them, such as I have heard my self
(with much grief, that have bin swearers, most notoriously, and have spoken of
the secrets of nature of Men and Women, in such a manner, as if they had never
lived where Gods Word had come to their knowledge, in such a manner as the very
Indians (that are civilized) are ashamed of, or not accustomed to; in such a
manner, as That their mouths are filled with cursing and bitterness,
destruction and calamity are in their ways, the way of Peace they have not
known.

I leave them, and speak to some other, I believe there may be many (some I
know) of whom I am persuaded I may safely affirm, That they are the elect of
God, and yet nevertheless through weakness (for so I judge it to be) do not
favor the Army and the present government; I hope God will show them just
cause to see their error, and to acknowledge it in this particular. But
concerning those that stand for the present government and Army, I know not,
nor have I discoursed with, nor heard of any one Man that has cordially
favored the proceedings of the Army and this present government, but they
appear to be either godly or civil, not openly prophain (I would not be
mistaken, I speak not in this particular what the Soldiery may be, I mean the
common Soldiery may be) I know nothing against them; but this I can affirm
upon my own knowledge upon inquiry, in Cornwall, and in Devonshire, they
behave themselves so orderly, that I much rejoiced to see their civil and
orderly carriage; and I did purposely enquire of the Inhabitants, and I
remember not any one but did acknowledge, that they carried themselves orderly.

To conclude my Answer to this Objection, I do acknowledge sin is committed too
openly in the sight of the Sun, there are many offenses. Let us all look to it,
for Christ Jesus the Son of the blessed God says that, woe be to him by whom
the offense comes. Certainly there is a righteous God that will prove and try
all our hearts and works, to whose righteous judgment I willingly refer the
Cause.

I humbly request those that fear God not to be offended, for consider that
many take liberty to the utmost to detract the Army, and present government;
therefore give me a little liberty. I would not exceed the bounds prescribed
by God. But to return to show cause why we may now expect Reformation Judges is
at the first: this following is the seventh Observation gathered from this
prophecy: namely, because God has stirred up many godly and learned, in these
times to put in writing what they have gathered from the prophesies of the
Prophets, and these jointly and unanimously do agree (so far as I know) that
near to these times God will do great things, such as have not bin done for a
long season) in reforming matters, in exalting, and lifting up his Church out
of affliction. This is an encouragement to us, to hope and expect, that we
shall have Judges as at the first, and counselors as at the beginning, then
shall we be a City of righteousness, a faithful City. Unto the foresaid
Scripture we may add that Esai. 2.2. It shall be in the last days, that the
Mountain of the house of the Lord, shall be exalted in the top of the
Mountains, and shall be exalted above the Hills, and all Nations shall flow
unto it: I leave this to your consideration. Read Dan. 7.24, 25, 26, 27. The
ten Horns that thou saw, are ten Kings that shall arise, and another shall
arise, Ver. 25. and shall speak words against the most high, and shall consume
the Saints of the most high, and think that he may change Times and Laws;
and they shall be given into his hand until a time, and times, and the
dividing of time. Ver. 26. But the judgment shall sit, and they shall take
away his Dominion, and consume it, and dectroy it unto the end: and the
Kingdom and Dominion, and the greatness of the Kingdom, under the whole
Heaven, shall be given unto the holy people of the most high, whose Kingdom is
an everlasting Kingdom, and all powers shall serve and obey him. From these
precious Promises or Prophesies recorded by the Prophet, I shall collect such
things as (I do conceive) do plainly arise from the Text.

First, that Kings should be enemies to the Saints and people of the most high,
and should do much damage to them during their government, and that they should
be lifted up in their own imaginations to think that they might change Times
and Seasons: by which, I conceive, is meant that they shall endeavor to govern
(not according to the prescribed rules of God, but) by their prerogatives
royal (as they term it) that is, according to what seems good in their
eyes, being beyond those limits which God has prescribed in his Law: this, I
conceive, is plainly held out in these expressions, and think that they may
change Times and Seasons: by Times and Seasons may be meant such things as are
already prescribed, by a higher power, within bounds, and by the wisdom of him
that had true authority to appoint such Rules.

Secondly, I observe that such corrupt Governors shall be destroyed and put
down by those that God in his wisdom appointed as instruments, to accomplish
his decrees. This is plainly held out in these expressions, And they shall take
away his Dominion to consume, and to destroy it unto the end, noted Ver. 26.

Thirdly, that now in these latter times God has determined, to restore and to
reform government, which (I conceive) is plainly held out in these
expressions. Ver. 27. The Kingdom and Dominion, and the greatness of the
Kingdom, under the whole Heaven, shall be given to the holy people of the most
high, whose kingdom is an everlasting kingdom.

Fourthly, that this prophecy is not yet fully accomplished, because it
appears plainly (to my best understanding) that from the Prophet Daniels time
to this time, the government under the whole Heaven was not yet given to the
holy people, and also because this Kingdom this government, or this power taken
out of the hands of the foregoing Kings, shall be everlasting, it shall
continue notwithstanding all oppositions against it, I leave these things to
due consideration. Read Micai 4.1. to 9. But it shall come to pass in the
last days, that the Mountain of the house of the Lord shall be prepared in
the top of the Mountains, and it shall be exalted above the Hills. Ver. 3, And
he shall judge among many people, and rebuke mighty people a far off, and
they shall break their Swords into Mattocks, and their Spears into Sithes,
Nation shall not lift up a Sword against Nation, neither shall they learn to
fight any more. Ver. 4. But they shall sit every man under his own Vine, and
under his own Fig Tree, and none shall make them afraid, for the Mouth of the
Lord has spoken it, Ver. 7. and the Lord shall reign over them in Mount Sion
from hence forth for ever. Ver. 9. Now why do thou cry out with lamentation
there is no King in thee, is thy counselor perished? for sorrow has taken
thee as a woman in travel. Ver. 12. But they know not the thoughts of the
Lord, they understand not his counsel; he shall gather them as sheaves in the
barn. Ver. 13. Arise thresh O Daughter of Sion for I will make thy horn Iron,
etc. This prophecy (I do conceive) is not fully yet fulfilled and completed,
for although it might have respect to the coming of Christ; yet it holds out
more matter then (as I conceive) yet is come to pass, because the prophecy
recorded that men should break their swords into mattocks, and their spears
into sithes, Nations shall not lift up a sword against Nations, neither shall
they learn to fight any more. This I conceive cannot be accomplished, because
if we understand it in any sense (I see not that) this is yet accomplished, but
is still to be accomplished. And for several other reasons here aledged, which
I leave to consideration. Read Revel. 11.15. And the seventh Angel blew the
Trumpet, and there were great voices in Heaven, saying the kingdoms of the
World are become the Lords, and his Christ's, and he shall reign for evermore.
From this place (I conceive) may be gathered that the governments shall be
reduced to such a method and form as God has prescribed in his holy Word,
according to the first and most immediate pure instruments. Read Revel. 14.8.
And there followed another Angel saying, Babylon that great City is fallen is
falen; Now we may note that Babilons confusion springs from this root, for
want of good Government; this is the very root of the sin and disorder, namely,
evil Government; for if we read the Records of the Kings of Israel, and take
notice, we may plainly see, That evil and corrupt Governors brought confusion
to and amongst the People; on the contrary consider, That in an orderly, and in
a rational way, when God will bring his people out of confusion into order, God
will certainly reform Government, that being the principal instrumental way of
Reformation; so then, when God foretells, That the Babel of Confusion shall
fall, this is a principal part of the meaning, namely, That corrupt Governors
must fall with or before it.

Time bids me forbear to multiply places, there are many godly and learned men
that have written largely and learnedly concerning Babele fall, to whom I refer
the Reader for further satisfaction, and shall conclude this Point with that
which is written, Revel. 18.8. Therefore shall her plagues come at one day,
death, and sorrow, and famine; and she shall be burnt with fire, for that God
which condemns her is a strong God: (Note I pray you in the verse before, She
sat as a Queen, and lived in pleasure;) Was not this draught much like the
picture of evil Kings? But Verse. 9. The Kings of the earth shall bewail and
lament over her: (Note, that the Kings of the earth are noted to lament and to
fear her torments: Why should they fear? Ans. Because a guilty conscience
causes fear, they being sensible that they have so slighted Gods Law:) which
have committed fornication, (note like fornication,) and lived in pleasure,
(note usually, that is one note, they lived voluptuously) with her, (these
words (with her) imply a near conjunction,) when they shall see that smoke of
that Her burning: Verse. 10. And shall stand afar off for fear of her torment,
(and why? Is it not because it threatened them?) saying, Alas, alas, that great
City Babylon, that mighty City, (is fallen, is fallen,) for in one day thy
judgment is come. Verse. 11. And the Merchants of the earth shall weep and wail
over her, etc. Verse. 17. And every ship-master, and all that occupy ships, and
ship-men, and whosoever trafique on the sea, shall cry, Alas, alas, that great
City, etc. is made desolate. But note I pray you what the blessed Servants of
God esteem of this fall of Babylon, this is noted, Verse. 20. O Heavens, rejoice
over her, and ye holy Apostles and Prophets, for God has punished her to be
revenged on her for your sakes. I pray you consider why the Prophets and
Apostles should in such primary and particular manner rejoice over her? Answ.
Was it not because she ruled by her prerogative, by her own will, and would not
be ruled and guided by the Writings of them, the Prophets and Apostles;
therefore the Prophets and Apostles (whose Writings this great Whore had
slighted) are noted in such a peculiar and eminent manner to rejoice at her
downfall

To conclude, (if she be falling or fallen) I hope God will keep me that I
shall not under-prop her to keep her up.

Thus (I believe) by this Babel of Confusion is plainly held out (by the
blessed Spirit of God,) That corrupt Government and corrupt Governors are to be
understood thereby, which Babel of Corruption must be put down, this being the
root (of confusion) must be plucked up by the very roots.

And further note, That the very true way to be beautiful and good order must
arise from good Government and good Governors, therefore if ever we do become a
City of Righteousness, and a faithful City, let us very circumspectly and with
all diligence) labor, that we may have Judges as at the first, and Counselors
as at the beginning; that is to say, as in the first, and in those most
uncorrupted times, when God did the most immediately appoint Government and
Governors: Let us keep close to Gods Rules, and then we shall not err.

Thus much briefly I have writ to show some grounds that strengthen me to
expect, That now in these latter times God will do some eminent matters in the
Reformation of Government, and (to my apprehension) these actings of God in
these times do hold out such a thing, namely, That God is exalting his poor
afflicted (and so much despised Servants and People.) I leave it to
consideration.

I shall, by the assistance of Gods good Spirit (which I hope and believe I am
guided by) now proceed to describe Government according as I find it
prescribed, owned and blessed by God, and recorded in the sacred Scriptures,
and as at the first in the purest times: Therefore, first, I find, That God did
begin the model, or the form, or the composition of Government at the head or
chief Ruler: Moses was the first, touching his entrance, he was called
immediately by God, and so were diverse others till Samuels time. And because
Gods presidents and doings are done in such perfect manner, with such wisdom,
and so exactly useful and fit for those employments that God disposes them
unto; therefore I conceive it may not be unuseful to commend something to
consideration touching this man; and first God sets out or describes his
parentage, Exodus 2.1. There went a man of Levi, and took to wife a daughter of
Levi: Verse. 2. And the woman conceived, and bare a son, (which was Moses.) Here
God does not describe any great difference between his parentage, and the
parentage of the rest of those people that God called him to govern. The like
is noted in the rest of those Judges which God did immediately call, and in the
best of Kings, David, who was a man God did immediately in mercy appoint to
govern his people Israel; this David, the best of the Kings, was chosen by God,
and taken (not for his eminent kindred, but) out of a low condition. From hence
I observe, That God does not look or choose Governors out of or by respects, as
man usually does: Man usually looks upon the outward man, this was Samuels
error; man looks at beauty, riches, kindred, rich or great parentage, at
eloquence, and the like, which respects usually lead men to choose those men
that prove usually neither any great promoters of Gods Glory, nor of the
Peoples good. God looks at the inner man, at the graces of his own Spirit in
their hearts, and principally God looks at his own Institutions, when such a
man is made Judge as enters into his office and charge purely according to
Gods Institution, ^o as God in his Word has prescribed, then God blesses such
with his Spirit. It is remarkable, that Moses pleaded his insufficiency for
that work God appointed him unto, (recorded for our learning,) Exodus 4.10.11.
Then the Lord said unto him, Who has given the mouth to man? or who has made
the dumb, or the deaf, or him that sees, or the blind? have not I the Lord?
Therefore go now, I will be with thee.

This consideration holds out to us, of what high and great concernment it is,
to observe with carefulness and diligence how our Governors enter in, and take
their offices and charges in Government; we cannot be too circumspect in this
matter, let us keep close to those first, most pure and unblemished directions
that God has most immediately prescribed, that are most clearly revealed in
his sacred Word, for that is our most certain guide, and the most sure way to
our future safety that possibly we can attain or reach unto.

It is very observable, That of all the Judges that God did immediately choose
(I cannot find) but that God endowed them all with his good and blessed Spirit,
and not one of them but proved to seek Gods Glory, and the Peoples good, from
Moses to Samuel, which was so long as the people followed Gods Institution in
their Government.

And observe well, That so soon as the people were negligent in following those
first and pure Institutions, most clearly and primarily prescribed by God,
concerning Government, then God did withdraw his gracious presence from them,
and what misery and affliction followed to them, and to their posterity, God in
his sacred Wisdom has left recorded (for our learning) in the Books of the
Chronicles and Kings of Israel and Judah: How did these Kings draw the people
from God into sin, and brought the fierce wrath of God upon the people? And did
not all this proceed from this root (namely from this) Because they were
negligent in the circumspect observance of Gods Prescriptions, and because they
leaned to their own understandings, and followed their own inventions.

Oh that we, the People of England, might now be wise, and learn (by our own
and other men's harms) to cleave close to the most pure, most immediate, and
first Institution of Government, recorded in the sacred Scriptures, so should
we secure our selves and posterity, and obtain a blessing and protection from
the glorious God of our Salvation.

Oh dearly beloved, consider I pray you, now there is such an opportunity as (I
believe) God never offered to any generation, from the days of Samuel to this
present time; now I pray you seek Gods favor, seriously put forth your best
and utmost endeavors, that we may obtain Judge as at the first, and Counselors
as at the beginning; then shall we be called a City of Righteousness, a
faithful City, Isa. 1. by this means we shall become good examples to our
neighbor Nations, and the generations to come shall have cause to praise the
Lord for us, and the memory of our names recorded in Gods Records shall be
eternally blessed.

Concerning this man Moses, being the first president God set to be Governor to
his Church and People, because Gods Works are most perfect, and of most
singular use to posterity, therefore I judge it necessary to note somewhat
touching his qualifications, he was a man painful and diligent in his charge,
he sat to judge the people from morning to night, Exodus 18.13. and afterward
in all his life we may note how studious he was, and diligent, and active in
observing Gods Commandments, and in exhorting the people to the same matters,
he was not ambitious to seek great offices and preferments for his own children
after his decease; which may be noted, when Israel the people had highly
provoked the Lord, so that God threatens to destroy the people, and promises
Moses, that he would so far prefer him, that he would make of him (that is, of
his posterity) a mighty people, Exodus 32.10. Now therefore let me alone, that
my wrath may wax hot against them, for I will consume them, but I will make of
thee a mighty people. Now Moses prefers the Glory of God, and the Peoples
good, before any by respects, either to himself, or to his posterity, noted
Verse. 11.12, 13. But Moses prayed unto the Lord his God, and said, O Lord, why
does thy wrath wax hot against thy people which thou have brought out of the
Land of Egypt? etc. Wherefore should the Egyptians speak and say, He has
brought them out maliciously, to slay them in the Mountains? etc. Turn from thy
fierce wrath, and change thy mind from this evil toward thy people, and
remember Abraham, Isaac, etc. Verse. 14. Then the Lord changed his mind from the
evil which he threatened to do unto his people. This is recorded for the
learning of succeeding ages, to show of what concernment and what benefit the
people get by living under such a Government and Governors as God sends; such
Governors stand in the gap to keep off Gods displeasure, and to procure a
blessing for the people. Many respect not much under what Government they live,
this was Lots sin, who deeply tasted of the cup of Gods displeasure by living
under or amongst the ungodly in Sodom.

But secondly, This example of Moses is of singular use, an eminent pattern to
all Governors succeeding, namely this, That he sought Gods glory, and the
Peoples good, before his own or his childrens preferment: It is to be noted the
like of him when God told Moses he should be taken away or dye, he does not
request of the Lord to continue the Government to his children, but this he
does, he loves the people, he looks at Gods glory, and the peoples good,
therefore he remembers the peoples good, and makes earnest prayer (recorded
for our learning) to God, entreating God, That he would appoint a Governor for
the people; where note the modesty and humility of his heart, his spirit being
not lift up above his brethren, therefore he expresses it thus, That he may go
in and out before the people, that the Congregation of the Lord be not as sheep
without a shepherd: Where we may note, That he styles himself and successor
but under these expressions, Number. 27.16. Let the God of the spirits of all
flesh appoint a man over the Congregation. Verse. 17. Who may go in and out
before them, and lead them out and in, that the Congregation of the Lord be not
as sheep without a shepherd: Note his expressions, A man over the Congregation,
(not only a King, or by the name of Commander, but) only a man, and a shepherd;
he had true respect and understanding of the nature of his charge and office,
which was to order, to provide for, to feed, love, and defend the stock, (and
not to persecute, or to suffer Wolves to devour them, not to feed upon them
himself,) therefore note his expression, Verse. 17. that the Congregation of the
Lord: He remembered and modestly acknowledges the people to be Gods heritage;
He does not style them his Subjects, or his Vassals, (and so seek to leave the
people, as inheritance of Goods, Lands, Beasts, and Cattle, to his Children,)
but he esteems the people, and so they were (of more value then earthly
inheritances) Gods inheritance; and so in express words he calls them, The
Congregation of the Lord, the Lords Inheritance, the Lords People; and
therefore he does not lay claim to them as the Inheritance for his Children, he
knew Gods mind better, he speaks no such matter; for succession in Government,
from the Father to the Son, came in long (many hundreds of years) after, in
more corrupted Times; God did not, in these first and purest Times, in the
original, order it to be so; neither did Moses expect, or desire it, because he
looked after those matters that were truly his own; He truly sought Gods Glory
and the Peoples good: But thus much to show his opinion and respect that he had
of the people in those days. Those first Governors owned the people to be their
brethren, and so they behaved themselves toward the people as brethren: Is not
the World much altered in these days, when many great men will scarce
acknowledge the poor people to be any of their kindred afar off, much less as
brethren? Yea, this Governor, in these first and purest Times, did not only use
the People as brethren, but as children, he carried them in his bosom, near his
heart, (and tenderly too) as sucking children; and that also by Gods own
direction, as Moses himself witnesses, and willingly acknowledges: But when
Kings obtained the Government, we may observe how soon the case was altered,
Abimelech he slays his brethren, that he might obtain the preeminence; and
Saul he persecuted an innocent and virtuous man, fearing lest he might hinder
his son from reigning after him; yea he pursues this with such violence that
he makes little account of Gods Commandments, if they stand in his way to
hinder him to make sure the Government to his son Jonathan, blood is not much
valued in his sight, witness the death of Gods Priests, 1 Samuel 22.19. And Nob,
the City of the Priests, smote he with the edg of the sword, both man and
woman, both child and suckling, both Ox, and Ass, and sheep with the edg of
the sword; and David's life, which he earnestly sought: Witness his unjust
molestation of the People, whom he forced from their own dwellings to pursue an
innocent and good man: These were some of the first fruits of their Kings, more
followed afterward; But thus it was not the practice of these Judges in the
first and purest Times.

But further we may note, That this man Moses and his successors (to the days
of Samuel) such as God instituted (I do not mean such as crept in at the
windows, and in bypath, not in the way God instituted) but Moses and the rest
of his successors to Samuel, we read much recorded concerning their virtues,
their pains, and diligence, but we do not read that they addicted themselves to
gather great Estates to leave to their children (and such as they had fleeced
from their brethren the People unjustly) nor do we read much of their
banqueting houses, nor of their sumptuous palaces, nor of their numerous
servants, nor of their hunting and hawking, nor of their excerable swearing and
blaspheming the great and glorious Name of the Lord, nor of their Prerogatives
Royal, to overtop and annihilate Gods Commandments, and to seize upon the
wracks of poor distressed Merchants and Seamen, which suffered shipwreck upon
their borders; a custom, I believe, hateful and abominable in the eyes of the
Lord, and directly in opposition to his Commands, who commands us to help and
relieve the oppressed and afflicted, and not to strive to add to their
afflictions, by taking away that little that God had otherwise spared to them.
(I heard of one ship since my arrival, that the people seeing themselves in
danger, forsook the ship, yet after this ship was so brought to the shore, that
much of the loading (being rich, and of value) was saved from the violence of
the Sea, but not returned to the Owners* that I could yet learn:) I humbly
entreat you that are our Governors, make diligent enquiry, that no more such
crying sins be committed, lest it bring upon us the fierce wrath of the Lord.)
But to return; Neither are these Judges noted to keep a company about them of
swearers or other vicious persons, such as I here name not, but such as your
ears have heard of, and such as God abominateth. These Judges, in these first
and purest Times, were humble, faithful, watchful, and pious men, men whose
acts are recorded by Gods direction to all generations, that they might be
examples to follow.

[O Lord,] shall we ever live to see those, (or such as those Governors that
were in those first and purest times?) Have thou given us hope of such a
Reformation? Blessed be thy Name; I believe thou have promised, that we shall
have Judges as at the first, and Counselors as at the beginning; then shall we
be called a City of righteousness, a faithful City.

Having spoken thus much (although it be very much less then the scripture
records for our learning) touching the qualifications and virtues of these
Judges in these first and purest times, wherein God did the most eminently and
the most immediately appoint and prescribe Government and Governors, to and for
his Church, and peculiarly chosen people Israel; I shall now endeavor to
propound to consideration (according to the measure of grace received) to draw
out of Gods sacred Word what find there recorded concerning the principal
Governors and other Governors distributed in several administrations, and also
their power and limitations, and also the entrance of them into their places.

I find, That God, in his divine wisdom, saw it meet for his Church, and
chosen, and peculiar people, to ordain, institute, and appoint one chief Judge,
and not many: Thus it appears in the book of Exodus, and in the records of
Joshua, and of all the Judges, and in the book of the Kings, that one chief
Judge had the charge: for although Judah and Israel were divided, it is there to
be noted, that afterward they became as two distinct and differenced
Governments: and also we note, that this was not so in those first and purest
times, wherein God did the most immediately and clearly appoint Government: And
also we may observe, That this division did not strengthen them, nor did it
turn to their peace and welfare, as afterward appeared, and is recorded in the
Books of the Kings and Chronicles; For although God suffered it to be so, yet
we may also consider, That God suffers, and brings upon the people for
their sins, many trials and afflictions, which yet God knows how to make use
of for his own glory: This people would not keep within the bounds of Gods
first institutions, therefore God causes them to see the difference of
Government, to see the difference between his prescriptions and institutions,
and their own inventions: and also, that God might show the fruits of such
irregular proceedings to us that should come in these latter times; Whatsoever
was written, was written for our learning: Considering this, I dare not turn
aside from Gods Commandments in those first and purest times, wherein God
appointed, that there should be one Governor, and but one as chief.

And that this is the best way of Government, most for Gods glory, and the
peoples good, these Reasons guide me thereunto.

First, Because God in his wisdom did see meet that it should be so; witness
the immediate pattern God gave to the people, Moses, Joshua, Gideon, Samuel,
and the rest.

Secondly, Because this is the pattern of that glorious Government in Heaven,
one God distinguished, but not divided in three persons, which governs over
all. God inviteth us to be like to himself, and seteth forth himself for us to
imitate; Be ye holy, for I am holy, says the Lord, (a place well known,) From
hence I conclude, That that Government is best that is most like, most
conformable, to Gods Government in Heaven.

Thirdly, We know that Forces united are strongest, and occasion less
difference and discord: We may see in the Records of our own Nation the many
Troubles, Wars, and Discords that many several Governments brought forth and
produced. If men should commit the constant Government of a Land into many
hands of equal authority, call them by what names you will, would not this be
the issue and fruits thereof? First, They should turn from the first and most
pure way prescribed by God, (which God forbid:) And also would not such
Governors be themselves over burdened with business? and would not the People
be worn away, wearied and oppressed thereby? It was Jethroes counsel to Moses,
and the Lord allowed or approved of it, namely, that there is recorded, Exo.
18.18. Thou both weariest thy self and this people that is with thee. Verse. 21.
Provide thou among all the people men of courage, fearing God, men dealing
truly, and ha^ing covetousness, and appoint such over them: Verse. 22. And let
them judge all small matters; so shall it be easier for thee, etc.

We may there note, That this distribution of Justice into many hands was not
to the intent that many should judge ordinarily in every one case, for then it
would have brought both a greater burden upon Moses, and upon the people,
because when the judgment of a cause goes through many hands, these many
hands, or Judges, are with more difficulty brought together, and with greater
charge, greater expenses; and likewise their judgments not easily reconciled:
And also such cases, in such a manner heard, are longer in issuing, fewer
causes can be heard, and likewise the people will be burdened with long
waiting, and great expenses to maintain this ch^rge: Therefore there were not
more Moses's added, not more Governors of equal authority to assist Moses in
the hearing such causes as came ordinarily to be judged by him: But it is
evident, That this multiplying Judges was to that end, that these Judges, or
Rulers, being chosen, might be distributed into the several Tribes where the
People lived, to the intent that the People might not travel far, but might
have their causes tried and judged near to their own habitations. And this did
not weaken, or lessen, nor diminish from Moses his authority, there was this
still reserved, that Moses the chief Judge should still have the sole judgment
and determination of the weightiest matters and affairs. This further
appears by the extent of Joshua his authority, Joshua 1.16, 17. Then they
answered Joshua saying, all that thou command us we will do, and
whithersoever thou sendest us we will go: as we obeyed Moses in all things, so
we will obey thee: only the Lord thy God be with thee as he was with Moses.
Ver. 18. Whosoever shall rebel against thy Commandment: and will not obey thy
Words, in all that thou command him, let him be put to death, etc.

Here it may be noted that the chief judge or governor, that was over Gods
heritage, had power to command and to determine all the weightiest matters that
concerned the people of the Lord.

If we look but upon a Family, (which represents a little commonwealth) we
shall there find that God appointed one chief governor: (although the woman
be in such a relation) yet God knew that it was meet to ordain one to be
chief governor, whose word should be of force. This does avoid much
contention, where it is willingly consented unto by all in the Family. But on
the contrary where the wife (which is the nearest relation and the most eminent
in the Family next to the man) does contend for the guidance of all matters in
the Family, What sad events do follow in such cases? That mutual love that
otherwise would be between the Man, and the Woman, is separated, the Family
disturbed, servants and children grieved, neighbors offended, and God much
dishonored. Even so and much more (I believe) we shall find the Commonwealth
to be disturbed, where no one is chief.

Object. But is it not said, that in the multitude of counselors there is
safety?

Answ. That shows that the chief governor should not be so proudly lift up
in his spirit, that he should despise the advice of others, in which respect
David shows an humble frame of heart, when he says that he will not reject
the advice of his servant, much more not of those that are in nearer relations.
It is a precious virtue to be of an humble frame of heart, to hear the counsel
of others: but this does not destroy the lawful authority of Order in
Government.

Touching Parliaments, or Assemblies of the Elders of the people doubtless (I
conceive) they may be, in diverse cases, as in the case of the defect and want
of a chief Judge, or in case that the chief Judge shall degenerate and
decline from the Institutions and Commandments of God, they are ordained and
approved of by God in such cases and in other cases, provided that they do not
diminish the power and lawful authority that God does allow to such good
governors that walk in his ways. This appears by that quere that the
Prophet Samuel makes to the People, when he demands, 1 Samuel, whose Ox have
I taken, or whose Ass have taken, or whom have J done wrong unto, or of whose
hands have I taken any bribe to blind my eyes therewith? as if he should have
said, if you could justly lay to my charge these things, there might be some
just cause, wherefore you should come together to demand another governor
(although neither would this warrant you to change the form of government, for
therein you should break Gods institution.) This appears likewise when the
people assembled to depose and punish Athaliah, and diverse others: and the
reason is plain, because God must be honored above al, he is the supreme
governor, and ruler of rulers, and people

Doubtless that Law of God that binds all men (without respect of persons)
to the observation of it, must of necessity find a way, and allow a way for
the observation of it, otherwise it would fall short in the perfection of it;
but to say that God only must punish chief governors for their offenses in
another world, to me plainly appears to be of no validity, for God gave the
Laws to Men on Earth to be observed, and the breach of his Laws to be
punished upon earth, without any respect of persons or limitation, and one Law
of God binds all men.

But to return, that lawful power, and authority, that God gives; and has
been given and yielded to all good governors (by Gods Church and People) must
doubtless be yielded to all good governors in like relations, and with the
like respects: therefore I believe this is evident from the whole premised,
that the principal governor of a Commonwealth must be one, and must have
neither less, nor more authority then Moses and Joshua had, in those first and
purest times of Gods institutions: And because we have the like liberty to
punish or to remove such offenders as break the Law of God that they had: if we
see that such chief governors do evidently act to Gods dishonor, and the
Peoples ruin, (which are unseparable companions) Gods Laws do help the
people, in case that God give the people hearts to improve them to his glory.

Do but warily cleave to Gods ordinances, to his institutions. Let the chiefest
governor be subject to the punishment that God prescribes in such cases, for
such offenses in his sacred Word.

Secondly, let none succeed by succession, from Father to Son.

Thirdly, take heed that God choose governors, let them be of his sending, and
this is of more validity, (then all the ties, fetters, charters, acts, and what
ever inventions of man) to secure Gods glory, and the good of us, and of our
posterity, (as I believe); for our danger and misery arises from this root,
namely, when governors creep in at the windows, and in by-pathes, and are not
indeed true Shepherds, but Wolves and Foxes: and shall we love them so well,
that we shall take them by succession; and not enquire of God, who shall be the
man? thirdly, if we are yet more negligent, so that when they appear to be (as
they too often prove) Wolves in sheep clothing, yet do we observe Gods Laws,
which lays such open to punishment?

The reason seems to me to be evident that caused the People, from time to
time, to use such pains, and diligence, to obtain from former Kings, grants,
that the Kings should not oppress, or tyrannize over the People, or their
consents to several such Acts in Parliament; was it not because the Law of God
was kept in obscurity? (the time fore determined by God, was not then
accomplished) who, or where was the man that durst, or did so far adventure, to
declare the Law of God in that particular; namely that Kings were subject to
the Law of God according to the true latitude of it; for had the Law of God bin
fully, plainly, and clearly opened, the People might easily have seen, that
they had had less need of such promises, because the Law of God is a more
strong, a more clear, and shining light, then all the Laws of man whatsoever.
And was not this the very grounds why it came to pass, that notwithstanding
all the grants that the People could obtain from former Kings, they proved too
weak to hold down their loftiness. Witness queen Mary: did not she and many
others break the Laws of God, and draw the poor people to Idolatry, and take
away the lives of the poor servants of God, notwithstanding, all the Charters,
that the People had obtained in former Ages?

Was it not because the People were kept partly in fear of their great
overtopping power? and partly by reason they were kept in ignorance that the
Kings (and great men of the earth were equally without respect of persons)
subject to the Law of God, and most especially because (Gods time
fore-determined for the Reformation of government not being fully completed)
the People did not see (nor cleave steadfastly to) Gods prescriptions, to the
way God in his word appointed, for the calling of governors, but on the
contrary the People were careless and negligent in the matter of governors,
they made too light account of governors, not thoroughly seeing it to be of any
great concernment; and did not God so withdraw his good Spirit of illumination,
from the People, that he denied them wisdom, power, or opportunities, to
punish offending governors? Dearly beloved suffer this truth of God to be
fully and freely opened, and I believe, we shall not need to fear to set up
one as chief. And this likewise will be beneficial to us, for by this means
we shall not have so much bloodshed, for to obtain Crowns and Kingdom^^.

I pray you further to consider, that if a people should set up government
composed of many heads, or many members, making or head, or chief, having all
equal authority (in the steed, or for the want of one chief, governor) and
if this should be their places, their power, and actings; constantly to judge,
and determine, the affairs of a Commonwealth, this must needs be considered
that they likewise are subject to err (yea are they not often times more
subject to err) and to break Gods Laws? Now in such cases of delinquency, must
not there be left a way open to punish them, which must be some other
invention, and will it not follow thus ad infinitum, multiply what numbers you
will?

Consider o^ the benefit that a People get by having one chief governor, from
this example: suppose there were a hundred thousand Men in a Campe^: and
suppose that there were one hundred Generals, over every thousand of Men one
General, and suppose that every one of these Generals had an equal
authority. and not any one to command in chief. Consider, would the Camp be
in greater security, because their Cheiftaines or Generals were many, no one
commanding in chief above the rest? No verily, but in much more danger
thereby, not only in regard of a common enemy, but also in danger of emulation,
and strife amongst themselves. And suppose further that these Generals should
agree, that no act should be done by any one of these Generals that should be
valid, and of force, without the consent of the rest; would it not follow that
the People thereby should be more burdened; because when they had a matter,
they could not have it ended without the consent of the whole, would not their
matters be longer in agitation, and obtained with greater charge and
difficulty* and it would be a great danger, trouble, and burden (not to be
borne) to the Generals themselves: let us therefore be exhorted to follow Gods
wisdom in this matter, I doubt not but that a Parliament or Assembly of
Elders may be of eminent use and benefit, to the People, especially in such
times as these, till matters be fully ended and settled, and after they may
assemble and meet, to that end that Gods Commandments may be observed by all,
and to question, and punish any governor for the breach of Gods Laws, because
God approves and blesses two or three that meet together in his Name, to do
Gods work: but is not the constant Government of the Commonwealth to be put
into the hands of one Man, and must not he have so much power as Joshua had,
and other good Judges of Israel? the more we strengthen the authority of a good
governor, the more it is for Gods glory, and for our comfort and safety.

Consider another instance, if a Merchant or a great Tradesman had many people
to deal with all, by reason whereof he has occasion to employ 20 or 40, men
under him to dispatch business, these are not to the intent that they shall
constantly act in every business, for then (if they had all equal authority,
no one commanding in chief) they would one hinder another, and business would
go more slowly forward. Therefore the end why he calls or takes more men to
help him, it is to the end that they may at once tend upon and dispatch
several occasions, and also these are all of them to be subject to the Masters
order, and all the rest orderly to be subject one to another. Thus did God
ordain one Moses chief governor to whom God committed the government, (which
did nearly resemble Gods government in Heaven) but through Man's weakness,
(not being able to act like God) therefore God permitted Moses to ordain other
Rulers inferior to himself, and those were distributed amongst the People over
thousands and hundreds and fifties and tenns. Whereby it appears that the end
was not that all those rulers should act, in the judgment of the same causes
that Moses acted in. Neither were any of those governors (much less were they
all) to have equal authority with Moses. This did further appear by the
authority that all the Judges of Israel had successively.

I do but labout to set before you, these instances; and it is because I am
not like (so far as I know) to have any more opportunity in this World to speak
in the cause, blame me not therefore if I propound these things to your
