consideration, for I and my posterity are like to be subject to what form of
government, you establish, and I evidently see that from Government will arise
great blessings (if it be such government as God approves, if it be such as
God has prescribed) then I know that the blessed Spirit of God will rest upon
such governors.

On the contrary I know that if you mistake in government. I do expect that
great afflictions will follow, and Governors not entering into their places
according to the Rule of Gods Word, I shall not expect that the gracious
Presence of God, will accompany them, And this I evidently see (by the records
of the Sacred Word of God, and by the experience of all Ages recorded) that
where government is corrupted, they are a means to draw the People from the
sincere worship of God, and they are a means to bring the Wrath of God upon
the People:

I doubt not but there are amongst you many wise, godly, and men precious in
Gods esteem, I pray God double the Spirit of his grace upon you; and direct you
to see much more of Gods mind, however let it not be grievous, if I put you in
mind of those things which you know, and which are plainly recorded in Gods
sacred Word. Moses put the People in mind of the same things often, and so did
Joshua, and so did Christ, and his Apostles. This is all that I can do by all
the instances or arguments I can allege, it is but only to persuade, or put
you in mind of what is already recorded, plainly in Gods Word which is a
bright shining light; all that I can say, (in comparison of Gods sacred Word)
is far short of the darkest night, compared to the brightest shining light of
the day, therefore all that draws me, (or is any motive to me) in this cause,
is this, namely, The records of the sacred Scriptures show such a Government,
and such Governors, God did prescribe, in such a manner, and they were blessed
by God, they were a blessing to the People, and the holy, good, and blessed
spirit of God was given to such. God in his wisdom did so appoint.

On the contrary I have observed (both from the Records of the sacred
Scriptures, and from the Records of all Ages, and from well considered
experience) that although the inventions of men, which swerve from the most
approved Rules of Gods Word, may have a fair show in some men's eyes, yet he
that well notes such inventions shall in the issue find Gall and Wormwood,
bitter fruits, and Gods good Spirit does not accompany such inventions, which
causes me to keep a loofe from Man's inventions, especially in such a weighty
matter, and of so great, eminent and high concernment, both for Gods glory, and
for the Peoples blessedness. I conceive we cannot possible be too circumspect,
nor cleave too close and steadfastly, to the most approved and blessed form of
Government, and Governors prescribed, owned, and blessed by God, and recorded
in the sacred Scriptures, for our learning. Dearly beloved Fathers I speak
freely, and willingly, and with more liberty of speech to you, because I am
persuaded that your heart^ do* really seek Gods glory, because I believe that
you seek not your selves, and have better learned to tread under foot these
trifles, these sublunary comforts, and do seek for an immortal Crown of glory
provided for those that seek Gods glory; you beloved know how to value Eternity
better then a moment, better, then this short span of time. Therefore I pray
you be not offended.

But further, where there are many Judges of equal authority (though Men
fearing God, and seeking Gods glory) yet in many, or in some causes, and most
especially in the most weighty causes, do not respects sway much? As namely,
loath to displease one another, and lothfully to discover themselves? Are not
numerous companies, having all equal authority, subject to emulation, to
jealousies, yea and sometimes to be so divided, that does it not sometimes
appear so violent, that it occasioneth civil wars? or contentions? I pray
you to consider mortal man is subject to frailty. Therefore seeing the
Heavenly frame of government is by one ^od, and unto Gods Word the whole Host
of Heaven is willingly obedient; and considering that that government that God
appointed ( in the first and purest times, when God most immediately appointed
government, to his beloved first borne, and peculiar Church and People)
considering that God appointed this form of government, namely, by one Man a
chief Judge, who had sole power to judge and appoint, and to determine the
weightiest causes; is not this the safest way to avoid confusion and
contention, and most like to be blessed. Herein indeed will lie the great
weight of all the matter, namely, that we cleave close to Gods Rules. that so a
Wolf may be prevented for getting into the sheep fold. For let us but seek
God in those ways he has appointed seriously, and heartily, and (I doubt not
but that) we shall obtain a blessing, a Man sent of God. And then let us never
fear, but God will accompany such a man, with his blessed Spirit. Did ever a
People seek GOD humbly (following GODS Rules) and heartily, and failed? I
believe no Record of Divine authority will demonstrate such an example, in such
a cause, so prosecuted.

Object. But was not this form of government, peculiar to the state of the
Israelites, is it not abolished, at the coming of Kings?

Answ. I desire every one that does unfeignedly desire to do Gods Will to be
wary of this Objection, and consider that it is too much for us to turn aside
from Gods Institutions; but to deny Gods Institutions, this is a sin of a deep
impression. How often does GOD bid us beware that we do neither add, nor
diminish? this being duly considered I answer.

First, this Order of government by Judges, in this manner, was Gods own
Order. God did most immediately appoint this Order.

Secondly, God did prescribe this, to his Church and People, before the Law was
given. Moses was appoin^ed, and had his power and place, and the rest of the
Judges were orderly distributed, before the Law was given, at Mount Sinai.

Thirdly, this order of government was continued, confirmed, and blessed
immediately by God himself under the Law.

Fourthly, this O der was further confirmed by GOD, when the People in the
Days of Samuel desired a Government by Kings, which appears in that GOD
plainly affirms, that the People cast God off when they altered this form:
and further it appears that God was the same long after, by the expressions
of the Prophets.

Fifthly, there was never any Government since* to this Day, to be compared
with this Government, nor so blessed by God, as appears by the Records of the
Chronicles, and the books of the Kings of Israel, and Judah: to which we may
add the experiments of all Ages.

Sixthly, Gods Wisdom is most perfect, and God is unchangeable.

Seventhly, this Order was never repealed in any Age to this day.

Eighthly, the Promises of God in the Scripture, do plainly show that when God
will have mercy upon his beloved People, it shall be showed the most eminently,
and apparently, by restoring Judges as at the first, and counselors as at the
beginning.

Ninthly, this government by one chief as head and governor does the nearest
resemble, that Heavenly frame of government.

Tenthly, consider who ever thou art that harbourest such thoughts, that such
thoughts do arise from unsound Principles, I believe, not well balanced
considerations. Because admit or suppose thou were left at liberty, now to
prescribe a form of government, what form of Government could thou invent?
Consider that God witnessed evidently and eminently, that (when God prescribed
government by Judges (in such order as Divine records do mention) this form
was better then any other Nation, had in the whole World. No Nation was so
blessed by God in those times that had Laws and Ordinances so righteous (by
which is meant Governors or Judges, and Laws to be their Rules) as God in
those first and purest times did prescribe to his first borne Son.

And further consider, that we are not now a separated People from the true
Israel of God, we are not strangers to those Laws which God, then in those
times, gave to them; but contrarily we by Faith in Jesus Christ, are ingrafted
into the true Olive Tree, we now are part of Gods household, and do subject to
all the Laws of Gods first borne Son, and though they were our elder
brethren, yet now also God has, in his rich abundant, and not to be
sufficiently expressed mercy, begotten us also to a lively hope, so that we
also are their younger Brethren.

Therefore for any man to conceive, that he could invent a better form of
government, then any in the World in those times had, and a better form of
government, then God himself did the most immediately prescribe, and own, and
confirm, and bless; such a man (if there be any such) had need to consider
this matter first very advisedly; least wanting wisdom, to prescribe and power
to uphould, and power to bless and prosper such his inventions, he should be
found to be an opposer of God himself, and likewise exalt his wisdom above the
wisdom of God.

The next matter I conceive it will be meet to propound to consideration;
other judges or governors, that are in order inferior to this chief Judge
before mentioned. Exodus 18.25. And Moses chose Men of courage out of all Israel
and made them heads over the People, Rulers over thousands, Rulers over
hundreds, Rulers over fifties, and Rulers over tens, Ver. 26. and they judged
the People at all seasons, but they brought the hard causes to Moses, for they
Judged all small matters themselves.

The end wherefore judgment or Judges were thus distributed, is to that
intent, that both the chief governor may not be over burdened, nor the People
over burdened, recorded Exodus 18.18. Thou both weariest thy self, and this
People that is with thee greatly: the end being duly considered, we may more
easily distribute the governors: Governors are suitable to this proportion to be
distributed into the several Shiers, Cities, Towns, and Places, where the
People live. (which plainly appears the end being considered) for the very
affection of a loving Father is so prevalent, that love causes him to seek the
comfort of his children, and to provide for their comforts, and conveniences;
to this purpose the Apostle says, that he is worse then an Infidel that
provideth not for his Family. Now consider that the Commonwealth in some
respect, is the Family of the chief Governor.

It is a lamentable case to consider, have not the People bin, (I could wish it
were not so still) forced to travel many miles, to their great detriment, for
to get those causes decided, and determined, that might with much ease, have
bin ended at, or near to their own dwellings. Yea moreover have they obtained
the determining or ending of their causes, without making many or diverse such
chargable journies, to the undoing of too many Men, Widows, and poor
Fatherless Children; have not many for want of means, bin forced to loose
their rights, and lawful maintenance? Consider of it dear Fathers, and now let
it be remedied, and doubtless God will shortly say unto you, well done good
and faithful servant thou have been faithful in these things, come be ruler
over more and better things, enter into thy Masters joy.

But on the contrary consider that oppression is a crying sin, God will
certainly hear the cry of the oppressed, the cry of old, and young, the cry of
the Widows, and of the Orphans, God will certainly hear them, God will do
it, for the Mouth of the Lord has spoken it. Therefore dearly beloved Fathers,
I humbly beseech you let Governors be distr^buted into the several Shires,
Cities, Towns and Places where the people dwell. And keep close to the rules
prescribed in these first and purest times; namely, let the determination of
causes be in proportion, to these first patterns, let not the end be neglected,
which is, that Gods Laws be observed, and the People may be eased. I pray you
to consider what is recorded concerning Samuel, that good and pious Governor,
he, rather then the People should travel far, did travel himself to the
places where the People dwelt. 1 Samuel 7.16. And Samuel went about year by
year to Bethell, and Gilgall, and Mispeh and judged Israel in all those
places. No doubt he appointed Judges all over the Land, that did judge the
people l kewise. I pray you to avoid multiplicity of Judges, being of equal
authority to judge at one tim^, in one and the same cause, I believe, it will
not be so much for the Peoples comfort, not so suitable to the first and most
pure institutions, and, I believe, t will be too great a burden to those that
should be Governors, in such causes, in such a manner constantly.

I do conceive that from that end of the multiplying Governors, recorded Exodus
18. which was to ease the People, and Moses, and that Gods Commandments might
not be broken; and from the acting and president that Moses left there
recorded, it appears, that many governors are needful in their several
places, but not many governors of equal authority, constantly to act in one
cause, and not in the weightiest causes more and most especially. My reasons
mentioned are gathered from the president and wisdom of God himself.

Now I shall proceed to describe that way, for the calling or entrance of th^se
governors into their places. Being a matter of the highest and greatest
consequence to us, next under God, we cannot possible use too much diligence,
nor too much intention, nor too much watchfulness in this matter; which does
so nearly concern the glory of God and the good of us, and of our posterity. I
find that God does desc^ibe a clear, evident, and great difference, between
the chief, or principal Judge or Governor, and the other Governors inferior
to them, in regard or respect of their callings, or of Gods sending them, into,
and unto those places of government; therefore I shall observe the wisdom of
God, who first ordains the head, or chief governor* and shall begin with the
chief Judge.

We find that God did himself immediately appoint Moses, Exodus 3.10. Come now
therefore I will send thee unto Pharaoh, that thou may bring my people the
children of Israel out of Egypt. Ver. 12. And certainly I will be with thee,
etc. Here is Moses call: so likewise God did immediately appoint Joshua. Read
Joshua. 1.1. Now after the death of Moses the servant of the Lord, the Lord
spoke unto Joshua the son of Nun, Moses Minister, saying Ver. 2. Moses my
servant is dead, now therefore arise go over this Jordan, etc. Read. Number.
27.18. And the Lord said unto Moses take Joshua the son of Nun in whom is the
spirit, and put thine hands upon him, etc. We may note here that in the Verses
before, Moses did earnestly entreat God, that he would appoint a Governor, or
Shepherd, to go in and out before the people; Moses knowing of what concernment
it was to Gods glory and the peoples good, that the people should have a good
shepherd, note that God does not presently answer Moses thus, let the people
choose a Governor themselves; but on the contrary, God owneth this way, of his
own prescribing, as appears, because as God did immediately choose Moses, as
is before considered, so also here again God proceeds as before, and does
immediately choose Joshua, to be the chief governor of his people.

And secondly we may observe, that God gives this further manifestation of his
mind, in these words, in whom is the spirit, wherein, and whereby God shows,
that the People might have erred if they had chosen, for they could see but the
outward man. But God knew exactly who would be for his glory and for the
peoples good, he knew in whom his blessed spirit was. Next read Judges 1.1.
After that Joshua was dead the children of Israel asked the Lord saying, who
shall go up for us, against the Canaanites. We may here note, that the people
had bin so well instructed in the days of Moses, and Joshua, that they did
account it to be Gods Will, and their duty, to let God choose their chief
Governor; no doubt this people did not do this unadvisedly, but upon knowledge,
and due consideration, that it was the Will of God; and that it was the most
surest, and safest way for them, that God should choose their principal
Governor for them. Therefore they used the means, they enquired Gods mind who
should govern them. And it is to be duly considered that this People (nor any
of their posterity) did never seek God in such weighty Causes, Humbly,
Heartily, Earnestly, but God did usually, mostly, if not always, condescend
unto them, and answer them graciously, whether they enquired Gods Mind by the
judgment of Vrim, or whether by lotts, I cannot tell; but God answered both
these ways, and God owned and prescribed both these ways; as appears by
Samuel his practice in choosing Saul by Gods immediate direction. 1 Samuel, etc.

We may note further, that the people are recorded by God, to be a people that
did cleave close to, and were observant of, Gods Commandments, Josu. 24.31. And
Israel served the Lord all the days of Joshua, and all the days of the Elders
that overlived Joshua, and had known all the works of the Lord, which he had
done for Israel. We may note that after this Generation, the people grew wanton
and forsook the straight, and pure ways of the Lord; therefore the Lord
delivered them into the hands of their enemies, Judge, 2.12, 13.14. But the way
that God helps them, is by raising up Judges, Judge. 2.16. Read Judges 3.9.
And the children of Israel cried unto the Lord, and the Lord stirred up a
Savior to the children of Israel, and he saved them, Ver. 10. And the Spirit
of the Lord came upon him, and he judged Israel. Here we may note, that it is
not a vain thing to seek the Lord, for although the people had done wickedly,
yet when they cried unto the Lord, the Lord hears them.

And secondly, we may note, that God owneth this way; that himself chooses
Government immediately. Thus we may read that God did immediately send Gideon.
Judge. 6.14. And the Lord looked upon him and said, go in this thy might, and
thou shall save Israel, have not I sent thee. I note that where God does
immediately send, or appoint government from the days of Moses, to the days
of Samuel God does not institute or appoint the Son, to succeed in Government,
next after the Fathers death; and this continued all the time of those first
and purest times, and those times wherein God did most immediately appoint
Government in favor, and in mercy, to his Church and People. Whereby it
plainly appears that succession from the Father, to the Son, was none of Gods
institution, in those first and purest Times.

God chose Samuel to be Governor, or chief Governor immediately; by which (and
by the former Governors mentioned before) it plainly appears that God did
prescribe, and own, and bless this way, it appears that it was Gods mind,
and will, to choose Governors himself immediately. The next way that God did
prescribe of choosing governors, was by lot; whereby God did immediately choose
the chief governor, recorded, 1 Samuel 10.19. Now therefore stand you here before
the Lord according to your Tribes, and according to your thousands. Verse. 20.
And when Samuel had gathered together all the Tribes of Israel, the Tribe of
Benjamin was taken, and afterward he assembled the Tribe of Benjamin according
to their families, and the family of Matri was taken, so Saul the son of Kish
was taken; and Samuel said, See ye not him whom the Lord has chosen.

By this place it plainly appears, That God did ordain this way for the
choosing the principal Governor namely by lots, whereby God is said to choose.
There were some Judges, the manner of whose choice is not so expressly recorded
(those most eminent) are such as God first raised up, and used as instruments
in more then an ordinary manner; such, for ought I know, may be made useful for
Gods glory, and for the peoples good, such as God has raised up to work
deliverances for the people, such as (in that respect) may be called Saviors,
and such as are men well known to be men of courage, humility, and p ety: We
find, That God afforded deliverances, protection, and peace to the people, by
such men as, for ought I know, were so raised up; this way is the nearest to
these most pure and immediate callings of Governors by God to their places in
those first and purest times. But this is not so safe and clear a way, (so far
as I understand:)

First, Because we read not, we cannot find it recorded, (that I can find, and
I have searched the Scripture with diligence,) that God did appoint the people
to choose that way: Consider, That those acts that the people did, are not
therefore Gods Commandments and Institutions, for then we must follow them in
many actions, which would be vain to conceive.

Secondly, The People may err, and are much subject so to do.

Thirdly, Gods Law is express, we may not add nor diminish, we may not turn to
the right nor to the left hand, to or from Gods Commandments.

Fourthly, I believe the promises of God lead us to choose most exactly,
according to the purest Institutions, noted in Isai. 1. I will (that is, God
will) restore thy Judges as at the first, etc. that holds out as in the
purest times, etc. Before I make Application of what is mentioned, touching the
calling of these chief Judges, I conceive it will be needful to answer an
Objection, which is this:

Object. May not the people choose chief Governors? did not the people choose
Jepthtah?

Answ. The exact manner of Jepthtah's choice is not so plainly described, but
that, for ought I know, they might have some further enquiry then is set down;
much we read not of Jephthahs acts, this is to be noted concerning him, That he
did such an act as no other Judge did, (that we re^d of,) namely, he vowed such
an unllimited and unlawful vow, as occasioned him to sacrifice his daughter,
(and so he did) which was the direct breach of Gods Command in a high degree.

But secondly, consider, That it is a safe way in dubious matters, (especially
in such eminent matters as do so immediately concern Gods glory, and the
peoples good) to walk by the plainest, by ^he most evident ways that God has
prescribed.

3. God says expressly with many threatenings, and many times, That we shall
neither add nor diminish from his Institutions: Now this is evident, That God
choosing immediately either by voice, by Prophet, or by lot, is Gods own
appointment, It is without denial or question: and God foreseeing that the
people would corrupt their ways, and break his Institutions, by desiring to be
governed by Kings, yet God was so jealous of his honor, and tender of the
peoples good, in the choice of the chief Governors, that he says expressly,
Deuteronomy. 17. Thou shall make him King whom the Lord thy God shall choose: Therefore
considering that we may neither add nor diminish, it is without comparison much
safer to choose by Gods plain Rules: For in both the Government by Judges, and
in the Government by Kings, it is to be noted, That God did immediately choose
Governors; and I cannot see that a people that will follow Gods express Command
and President, can avoid but that God (and not men) must choose the chief
Governor: It is expressed and recorded, That God raised up Judges, and made
them Saviors to the people; but because the manner how God raised them up, is
not so plainly expressed, therefore (I conceive) that it is the safest way to
follow the plainest and clearest ways, by which are plainly declared, the
manner how God did choose, and wherein God did act, own, and most eminently
bless; but where God raises up men, and makes them eminent Instruments for
his glory, and by them works deliverance to a people, in such a case I dare
not oppose it, doubtless, I believe, it is a way nearest to Gods immediate
callings, and nearest to the plainest Presidents recorded in the sacred
Scriptures.

Fourthly, If the people choose, they are subject to err and mistake, they see
but the outward appearance, and they may intend one man, and it may be a great
number carries the choice to another, or they may be mistaken in the man most
meet for Government, which will appear, if we consider, that Samuel, a wise and
holy man, was mistaken in choosing but amongst one man's children, how much
sooner may we be mistaken, when we, having less understanding then Samuel, are
to choose out of a multitude, and we may be overpowered by money, by friends,
by kindred, by beauty, by eloquence, by fraud, or force, or ways we know not of.

Fifthly, Experience may teach us, That people do err very often, and choose
those men to be their Judges or Governors, that prove direct enemies to them
and to their posterity; witness Abimeleck, and a multitude of others, recorded
for our learning, and for our instruction.

Sixthly, God never erreth, and he does bless with his holy Spirit men of his
own sending.

Seventhly, God complainenth of this by his Prophets, formerly cited, saying,
They had Kings, but not by me; Princes, but I knew it not.

From the premises may be gathered three ways, whereby Governors were in those
first and purest times chosen and ordained; two of them are very clear, the
third I dare not absolutely oppose, but leave it to the consideration of the
godly-wise-hearted: I shall propound to consideration somewhat touching the
particulars, and then make a general Proposition, to consideration, touching
all the three jointly, as God shall assist.

First, concerning the immediate Call of God by voice, or Prophet, or some such
way as God shall see meet; I know no place of Scripture that does declare, That
God will no more appoint Governors as at the first, as he did Moses and Joshua.

Secondly, This Prophecy, Isai. 1. holds out much, for these words [as at the
first, and as in the beginning] may (for ought that I know) be determined by
God, to be accomplished in the full latitude, namely, as in the time of Moses
and Joshua: That Prophecy, Dan. 7.27. (in these words) And the Kingdom, and
Dominion, and the greatness of the Kingdom under the whole Heaven, shall be
given to the holy people of the most High: This seems to me to import, That
God intends to do great things for his people in these latter times: Read
Micah 7.17. According to the days of thy coming out of the Land of Egypt, I
will show unto him mavelous things: This (to my apprehension) holds out, That
God will do mavelous things; God is not limited within bounds, he can do as
great things now in these latter times, as in the former times. Thus in other
places.

Thirdly, I believe, That (with limitation and submission to Gods good will and
pleasure) we may safely present our humble prayers to God in the Name of his
Son our blessed Savior, That he would be pleased to appoint our chief Governor
for us: The Lord was so far from rejecting the people, Judge. 1.1. when they
sought his gracious favor in this particular, that he graciously grants
their request; God doubtless will not be offended, when people, with the
greatest care and diligence, cleave closest to him; the Apostle wills us,
That in every thing our request should be made known unto God by prayer and
supplication.

Fourthly, This way is a way that God did most immediately act, appoint, and
practice* and bless, from Moses to Samuel, and God never repealed or
contradicted this immediate way of his; God is unchangeable: If the people
formerly cast off God, and therefore God removed from them, and hid his face
from them, they never turning to God to seek his face, being much hardened in
their sins; yet if God now give us hearts to repent, and to see the evil of
them, and of our selves, and to turn again, and to long, and lament, with an
earnest affection, to do Gods will, without turning to the right or to the left
hand, without adding or diminishing; and if we do humbly and unfeignedly seek
his favor, who can tell but God may fully answer our petitions? God has done
already so much for us, in opening a way to further us in this particular, as
has not been from the days of Samuel to these times: I believe I may safely
affirm it.

Fifthly, Consider what a rich jewel, what a precious favor we shall obtain,
in case that our good God hear our petitions, and do immediately appear in the
choice of our chief Governor, for then we shall be sure to have a true
Shepherd, (and not a Wolf in sheeps clothing,) then we shall be certain that
the good and blessed Spirit of GOD will rest upon such a man, (and not an evil
and deceitful spirit,) then the people shall be drawn to God, (and not caused
to forsake God,) then the people will be blessed of God by the means of such
Governors, then shall we obtain a man from the Lord, then shall we have Judges
as at the first, and Counselors as at the beginning: Consider I pray you, is
not this jewel, this precious favor worth the looking after? Is it not worthy
our most fervent prayers? Have we not safe Rules (and clear) to warrant and to
direct us to cry to God in this very case of Government? Did not Israel cry to
God, and enquire of God for Governors? Did not God himself prescribe and
practice this way to choose Governors himself most immediately? Are we not
commanded, that in every thing our requests should be made known to God by
Prayer and Supplication? Did ever a people return empty from God in such
seekings of God? Nay, is it not evident, that (usually, mostly, if not always
God answered graciously, and granted peoples request in this very case of chief
Governors?

Consider further, you have endured much trouble, war, and bloodshed about
Government, if we should now fall short, and mistake in our governors, then our
labor is lost, we are undone: But on the contrary, if we obtain a man from the
Lord, we shall have a rich recompense for all our former labors. Therefore let
us not lose such a precious favor for want of asking at the hands of the Lord:
Who can tell but God may immediately answer us in some way of his own
prescribing? however let us not fear, nor doubt, our prayers shall not be in
vain, they shall be kept in Gods good treasury.

Sixthly, Consider that if you should mistake in the form of Government, or in
the persons, (which must govern us all,) such mistakes are very hard and
difficult to be amended; for when a Government and Governors are established,
let experience teach us, that we may sooner be sensible of our misery (which is
not ordinarily taken notice of, nor truly discerned) then know how to be free:
we may cry out, but not be able to help our selves. It is a long time since any
man durst plainly show to his familiar friend, where his grievance lay, if it
concerned Government. Consider it warily, and deeply, and thoroughly, for the
glory of God, for the good of thousands, and that your posterity and your
selves may remember with joyful hearts, how you preferred Gods Prescriptions,
Gods Rules, Gods Presidents, and the true good and safely of your Nation,
before any other momentany, light, and vanishing deceiving respects whatsoever.

Seventhly, Consider that where people choose the form of Government and
Governors, they are most usually mistaken, because they can discern no more but
the outward appearance (and few amongst many can discern that) they know not
who God knows to be meet: kindred is a relation that in outward appearance is
of great force; but by that means Abimelech obtained the way to Government,
Judge. 9.2. Say, I pray you, in the audience of all the men of Shechem; Remember
also that I am your bone and your flesh. Verse. 3. Then his mothers brethren
spoke of him, in the audience of all the men of Shechem, all these words; and
their hearts were moved to follow Abimelech, for, said they, He is our brother.
But note what followed, Verse. 23. But God sent an evil spirit between Abimelech
and the men of Shechem; There you may read what misery and bloodshed befell the
people.

I would shortly note three things from this Example.

First, That even those that immoderately thirst after Government, are usually
unmeet men.

Secondly, It usually is a means for the hurt of such Governors, and usually a
means to shorten their own lives.

Thirdly, That it usually, mostly, proves very bitter to those very men that
prefer others for by respects; and it is very dangerous when people venture to
choose the principal Governor, and do not therein seriously enquire of God who
shall be the man that shall govern them: And as we have many examples in this
kind; so, on the contrary, we shall find them blessed that let God choose
their Governor in chief.

But further, Remember that Samuel was mistaken in the person (amongst David's
brethren) fit for Government; how much sooner may we be mistaken? How many have
been lifted to chief Governors places by kindred, by unadvised multitudes, by
fraud, by force, by eloquence, by beauty, by hypocritical pretenses; Therefore
I pray you suspect your own hearts, lean not to your own wisdoms; for although
Custom have overshadowed Truth from our view, for a long season, (so that Truth
looks so strangely, now we see it, that we can hardly believe it is Truth,)
yet now I pray you let us own Truth, lest, if he depart again out of our sight,
we shall not know him again: Therefore I pray you seek after Gods Rules of
Truth, take his counsel who shall be our chief Governor, and this benefit will
certainly follow, The good and blessed Spirit of God will rest upon that man.

Next concerning lots, this is a way that God himself prescribed (though at
some more distance) as appears 1 Samuel God directed Samuel that the people
should choose their chief Governor this way, namely, by lots; by which way the
Lord (and not the people) did appoint their Ruler: And Samuel no doubt had
respect to Gods prescribed Rule, Deuteronomy. 17. Thou shall make him King whom the
Lord thy God shall choose: whereby it appears evidently, that Samuel so
understood Gods will in that Scripture, that there was a clear difference
between God choosing a governor, and the peoples choosing a governor; therefore
he chooses a governor by lot, wherein and whereby God chooses: therefore Gods
direction and institution is, that God shall choose: This is most for Gods
glory, and for the peoples greatest safety. Lots are Gods own Ordinance, as
appears in many places, Josh. 7.17. So Joshua rose up early in the morning,
and brought Israel by their Tribes, and the Tribe of Judah was taken: And he
brought the families of Judah, and took the family of the Zarhites, and he
brought the family of the Zarhites, man by man, and Zabdi was taken: And he
brought his household, man by man, and Achan was taken. God could have showed to
Joshua, who was the man, so well as he showed to him that there was an offense;
but he causes Joshua to enquire his will in such a way as God had prescribed:
This shows, that in difficult cases God ordained that people should enquire
his mind by lots: and this Samuel knew, and therefore he enquireth Gods mind
by lots, in this very case of government; this was never repealed to this day:
for God is not yea and nay, God is not contrary or opposite to his own Rules:
This is certain, it is better and safer for people to be directed by God to
choose the man; yea, although God for our sin should be angry with us, yet even
in those causes it is better to fall into the hands of God, then into the hands
of man; and this David well considered, when he chose to fall into the hands of
God, and not into the hands of man: But further we may observe, That this was
the usual way (namely, by lots) that the people took, to enquire Gods mind in
weighty and difficult causes, as appears, Josh. 18.6. I will cast lots for
you here before the Lord: thus Verse. 8, 10. read 1 Samuel 14.42. And Saul said,
casts lots between me and Jonathan my son, and Jonathan was taken: Here we may
see that God appeared, and gave a true determination, and this was a way to
avoid strife: Read 1 Chro. 26.13. And they cast lots, both small and great, for
the house of their fathers: Here again we may note, That this use of lots was
to show what Gods mind was, and to prevent all jealousies or indirect means,
and to prevent strife. Read Nehem. 10.34. We cast lots for the offerings of the
wood, even the Priests, the Levites, and the People. Read Jonah 1.7. And they
said every one to his fellow, come and let us cast lots, that we may know for
whose cause this evil is upon us; so they cast lots, and the lot fell upon
Jonah: By this it evidently appears, that the people in weighty cases did
enquire to know Gods mind this way, namely, by lots.

Secondly, We may observe, That God does answer the people this way.

Thirdly, We may observe, That the lot did not err, nor fail to show, that
which the people sought to God for. Read Act. 1.24. And they prayed, saying,
Thou Lord, which know the hearts of all men, show whether of these thou have
chosen. Verse. 26. And they gave forth their lots, and the lot fell on Matthias.
This shows, that lots were not abolished, but they are now of the same use
that they were under the Law; this is an example of the Apostles, men in an
extraordinary measure guided by the good and holy spirit of God; and this was
written no doubt for our learning; this was and is a clear and evident
direction in the very case of governors, for the Apostles were Gods
Ambassadors, his own Witnesses, they were the Penmen of the holy Scriptures;
this matter was an eminent and a weighty matter, they chose but one of two: The
Reason is evident, because the nature of their cause required no more.

First, Because not any amongst all, although holy, would serve, they must be
men that had been the most noted to be eyewitnesses of what Christ had done
and suffered, and so that they had seen and heard those things themselves.

Secondly, The Apostles were present that had an infallible spirit.

Thirdly, This cause differs from the Governors of a Commonwealth, because God
in his wisdom ordered the Governors of a Commonwealth to be chosen by God out
of all the people: and I do conceive (with due and humble respect to those that
shall see Gods mind more clearly) that it is the safest way to follow the most
direct and evident Rules prescribed, owned, and blessed by God, in the same
cases: Now it evidently appears, that the Prophet Samuel (directed
immediately by God himself) did choose out of the whole twelve Tribes of Israel;
by that means God did fully choose (according to Deuteronomy. 17. to make him Governor
whom the Lord did choose immediately) in this very case of choosing the Governor
of a Commonwealth; for, in this case, this president by Samuel was a certain
and an approved president, in choosing the person that God saw meet to be chief
governor; This was not about the form of government, whether it should be by
Judges, or by Kings, for of that matter God showed his mind by Samuel before,
expressly witnessing against the form of government by Kings: but this was a
Rule to show how God is said to choose the person that he sees meet to govern:
I leave it to the consideration of the godly.

From these places before mentioned, first, I observe, That it plainly and
clearly appears, that lots were ordained by God, and that God owned them,
because God truly appeared, and truly gave answer by them, and because that God
blessed this way of his own devising.

Secondly, I observe, That the lot (when men cast themselves, or referred
themselves, wholly to, or upon God, in such cases) did never err, it always gave
a true direction, a true determination in all weighty causes: Search the
Scriptures, and it cannot be found, that the lot ever erred. Let not as fear
therefore to choose our chief governor by lot; for let us not doubt, God is the
same unchangeable God, yesterday, and to day, and the same for ever: Will not
this way compose all our differences? Will it not heal all distempers? Will not
this way end all our strife? Will not this way keep out all Wolves, and Foxes,
and other beasts of prey? Shall not we by this way return again to the Lord?
and by this means God shall be our King, his Laws our guide; by this means we
shall obtain a man from the Lord, and we shall be blessed, and Peace and Truth
shall meet together; and so shall we have Judges, in some proportion, as at the
first, and Counselors as at the beginning, and we shall be called a faithful
City.

Thirdly, Let us remember the great effusion of blood that has been shed, and
the great envies, hatred, malice, that is at this day reigning in the Land; Is
it not in every Country, in every City, in every Pa^ish? Nay, there are but a
few Families (comparatively) where there are not some breaches about this
matter; and what the issue will be, the Lord knows: If therefore there be any
bowels of pity, if you love Gods glory, if you be lovers of peace and truth,
then fear not to trust in God in this matter, God is not changed. Do we not
trust our Souls with God? and shall we not trust God with our Bodies? The Lord
give us understanding.

And now I shall speak a word to the third way of choosing Governors, it is said
in sundry places of Scripture that when the people had forgotten, or cast
behind them, Gods Commandments, yet even when they earnestly sought Gods
help, Gods counsel, then God stirred or raised them up a Savior, or
Deliverer. The way being not so plainly described, where we may take notice of
the peoples negligence in not seeking to God for Governors; for at such times
when the people committed such wickedness, (we shall usually find that) the
State or Commonwealth, was vacant of a chief governor. Read Judge. 3.7. So the
children of Jsrael, did wickedly in the sight of the Lord. Ver. 9. And when the
children of Israel cried unto the Lord, stirred them up a Savior, and he saved
them. Ver. 10. and the Spirit of the Lord came upon him and he judged Israel;
We may note here, that the people were negligent in inquiring of God before
their distress, for a chief Judge, the state was empty. And we may note that
till they sought the Lord, God suffered them to be afflicted, but when they cry
unto the Lord, when they do cleave to the Lord, the Lord relieveth them and
shows to them mercy this way, namely by stirring them up a chief governor.
And further we may note, that when God puts his spirit eminently in such a
person, then he judges Israel, no doubt but the Spirit of God came upon him in
some extraordinary manner. Read Jud. 3.12. Then the children of Israel again
committed wickedness in the sight of the Lord. (This was after the death of
their former governor) Ver. 15. And when the children of Israel cried unto the
Lord, the Lord stirred them up a Savior, etc. Jud. 4. The children of Israel
again committed wickedness. Ver. 3. And the children of Israel cried unto the
Lord: and we may there read how the Lord showed them favor by stirring up a
Savior. Where the Man was nominated that was their leader by the prophetess
Debora, but Debora at that time judged Israel* Ver. 4. And so Debora by Gods
appointment, I believe, judged Israel to the day of her Death.

The next was Gideon, Judges 6. He was immediately called, concerning diverse
Judges it is not so expressly noted, after what manner God stirred them up.
Whether it was by immediate Revelation, or by Prophets direction, or put his
Spirit into their hearts, and made them to be notable and eminent deliverers of
the people. In all such dubious cases, the safest way is to follow the most
evident, and clear Rules, Wherein, and whereby, God does most evidently
prescribe, own, and bless. Now consider, that Gods immediate call is clear
without all doubt, and choosing Governors by lot, is evident, and clear, to be a
way that God himself prescribed, and the lot never erred.

The third way is more dubious, yet I dare not oppose it, where God raises up
a man, and makes him an eminent deliver of his Church and people, if the
people in such a case choose such a man to govern them, God may blese it, this
way is left recorded in the sacred Scriptures, and we find that thus far God
blessed this way, that he made such Men (so raised up, or stirred up by God)
to become saviors, the people were protected, and not devoured, and the people
were blessed with peace in their days, this is the nearest way next to the
former, but in any wise take heed not to establish government by succession,
from Father to Son, we have tasted deep of the cup of affliction in this kind.
The Father a good man, the Child otherwise, the Father holding one opinion, and
the children another, this plainly appears from the Divine Records in the
Sacred Scriptures, and by the late sad experiences, in this kind.

We may plainly see the bittter fruits the people reaped, by Government from
Father to Son, if we consider and compare the fruits by Judges, with the fruits
that the people reaped by Kings, which succeeded by succession; Note well, that
the Government had continued from Moses to Samuel, which was many hundred
years, many generations; and yet we see God so blessed these Judges, that (came
not in by succession, but) were by God appointed where he saw meet, Read 1 Samuel
9.8. And the servant answered Saul again and said, behold J have found about
me the fourth part of a shekell of silver (which was about five pence, Read
Genesis 23.15.) that will I give the man of God to tell us our way: note well the
plainness, and godly humility, of the Judges in those times, that would accept
of five pence.

Note likewise, that in a short time when the Government, went by succession
from Father to Son, the case was altered, we may note in three or four
generations, the governors built stately houses, rich gardens, a thousand Wives
and Concubines, great multitudes of Charets and horses, these things were
directly against Gods Commandments, Deuteronomy. 17, In any wise he shall not
prepare him many Horses, neither shall he take him many Wives, neither shall
he gather him much silver and gold: but we may note, that Kings quickly
overtoped, and annihilated Gods Laws; This God knew, when God put a bit in the
mouth of Kings, to curb their pride, Deuteronomy. 17.18, 19. namely, Gods Laws, that
so their hearts should not be lift up: but these Laws would not hold them,
their hearts were above Gods Laws; God warned the People of this, the 1 of
Samuel, but the People would not hear till, they cried out under Rehoboam by
reason of their oppression, I believe a doorkeeper would not now accept five
pence.

Dearly beloved Fathers, if you should consent to government by succession, it
might be just with God, to let their hearts be lift up like to Rehoboam, that
God might make their little finger bigger then the former Kings loins, the
Father chastised us with rods, but the Son may with scourges. I pray you
therefore let us have plain, humble, blessed Judges as at the first (not
chosen by succession) but as in the beginning.

I shall now from these considerations make one general proposition (and humbly
lay it down at your feet, dearly beloved Fathers) which is, Considering the sad
and lamentable envy, emulations, strife, differences, that have been, and are
at this day in the Nation; may it not be meet, solemnly, after an extraordinary
manner, to humble our selves, and to cry unto our God for direction who shall
be our governor? It may be, before the time (which you set apart for this
occasion) be expired, God may reveal his mind in some extraordinary manner;
but if God appear not, then let us, within some little considerate time,
(before the time be ended, which God directs you to set apart for this work)
proceed to choose by lot; It is a safe way, it is a way God himself prescribed,
it never erred: Will it not be a way to remove all jealousies and subtleties,
and to compose all differences, and to put an end to all strife? But, dear
Fathers, I pray you however, in some convenient time, choose some one chief
Governor, eminently known for courage and for piety, and give him all the
lawful power that God in his wisdom, gave unto Joshua, and to other lawful
governors; This will be a way for Gods glory, and for the peoples (for us your
childrens) safety, and comforts, for Gods Wisdom is infinitely beyond all man's
inventions. I pray you let us not have a Titular Governor, if you shall not
think meet to condescend to any of these ways, I know whom I trust; and I hope
I shall show my self obedient, in all lawful matters, to such as God, and
you, shall see meet to appoint, and I shall not cease to entreat God so to
direct you with his good and blessed Spirit, that you may do that which is well
pleasing to him.

Now I conceive it will be meet to speak something touching those Governors
inferior to the former, which are for the glory of God, for the ease of the
chief Governor, and for the Peoples ease and comfort.

Now again I look upon the most glorious, perfect, and beautiful frame of
Government, which the blessed Angels do, (and the elect children of God shall)
enjoy to all eternity. Where I find one blessed God, the governor, and the rest
all appointed and distributed into their several places by the power, and
wisdom, of that blessed God. This leads me to conceive, that God
proportioneth his Works, like unto himself, for so God did in the Creation of
the World, and the creatures therein, God made one man governor of all the
creatures upon Earth, and that man named the Creatures, and disposed other
matters: it had bin man's happiness (provided that Gods glory had bin
maintained) that the government of the World, might have continued in, and
according to that lovely order. Secondly, God made that one man in his own
image, like to himself, and I believe we shall find that God composed, or
framed the Government of his Church, and People, in some proportion like to the
frame of the Heavenly Government: my time will not admit to speak much of that
blessed Spirit of God, part whereof God did communicate, or bestow upon Moses,
and so let him represent his place, so far as might stand with Gods glory, that
is so far as Moses might be subject to Gods Commandments, for therein God
reserved to himself his own glory, in Adam, the great Emperor, or governor of
the World. Yet he was subject to Gods Commandments; from these considerations
I shall proceed.

When God, in those first and purest times did appoint the distribution of
governors, recorded thus, Exodus 18.25. And Moses chose men of courage out of all
Israel, and made them heads over the people, Rulers over thousands, Rulers over
hundreds, Rulers over fifties, and Rulers over tens. Here I find that God gave
Moses authority, to appoint the governors, that were to govern the People.
Which authority, I do believe, does undoubtedly belong to all good governors,
being chief governors, only this is to be considered, that the People here
were ne^re to Moses, so that Moses knew many, or all of them. Therefore I
believe that God, that is the God of wisdom, and of Order, will allow, that
where People live further off, and the chief governor may not know all the
men, whose dwellings are further off from him, and therefore cannot so well
know the qualifications, and fitness of men for government, in such cases it
does much differ; but Moses must (I mean the chief governor must doubtless)
approve of all governors under him, that govern for Gods glory, and for the
Peoples good, ease, and comfort; There must be no inferior governor that he
approves not, for that would be directly against the frame of the Heavenly
government, and against the express letter of these first, and purest
institutions. And Moses must, I mean the chief governor must, choose
immediately (if it be possible with convenience) the chief next to himself,
namely the governors of thousands, this most nearely resembles Gods President.
God chose Moses, and Moses chose them under him, the words are express, and I
dare not alter them; I dare not prefer my wisdom, before Gods Wisdom, nor
dare I add, nor diminish, to or from Gods Prescriptions; the rest of the Rulers
of hundreds, fifties, and tens, may be chosen proportionable to this president,
(provided that the chief Governor approve of them.)

Now that this way, is most for Gods glory, and the Peoples good, appears, if
we consider that government distributed resembles, or supplieth that defect of
man; who cannot be every where present, nor here all causes (for otherwise they
all represent but one entire, and absolute governor) therefore God appointed
one chief governor, namely Moses, like to himself; but through the occasion of
man's weakness, to supply that defect, God suffers the Government to be
distributed.

Secondly, it appears that this is the best way, that the chief governor
should appoint (or at the least approve) the rest, because the Wisdom of God
saw meet it should be so, as is expressly recorded.

Thrdly, consider that it does strengthen, uphold and knit together the whole
frame of Government, forces united are the strongest.

Fourthly, it does prevent divisions; and may be a means to reform abuses,
when inferior governors are offenders, thus God when he sees his Laws
broken, does remove, and punish delinquents. For if you should admit of
governors against the mind and approbation of the chief governor, it must
needs follow, that that State so doing, must be corrupted, divided, or sore
shaken, and endangered, in short time; for let but Gods Laws take place, and
then the governor in chief is subject alike with the rest, and the rest acting
for God, have power to punish him, because God is their highest governor, and
they must obey God although it be against the chief of men. Therefore the
danger cannot be great thereby, but on the contrary, it is for Gods glory, and
for the peoples good, that the chief governor should appoint, or approve of
the rest, at the least.

Fifthly, it will appear to be Gods appointment, by the Records in the sacred
Scriptures, not only in the first institution (which is the best, and the
surest) but also in the continued practice of chief governors, all along, from
time to time. This appears Joshua 1.17. As we obeyed Moses in all things, so
we will obey thee, but Moses had the authority, to appoint governors; therefore
Joshua had so, and it appears by Joshua his actings afterward.

Thus we may read that Saul, and David, did appoint governors, recorded in
many places, and so did the Governors, and the Kings of Israel and Judah.

I shall refer these matters to the consideration of the godly, and of the
learned, if any lust to be contentious; I strive not to contend, but contend to
be quiet, and seek for Peace, and Truth.

And now I conceive it is requisite to speak a word, touching the Lawyers.
Gods Laws if we observe them well, are pithy, and short, they are contained in
a little room, if we substract the Historical matters, (or matter which show
Gods actings, and man's actings, which are not so properly Laws, but rather
show Gods glory, and man's conversation) from the direct Commandments of God;
in what a little volume, would Gods Laws be contained? which shows the
purity, and excellency of them, of Gods Laws.

The Laws of some Countries contain great Books or Volumes in comparison of
Gods Laws, many Lawyers look much upon the Letter of the common Laws, I
would there were many more looked faithfully to the true meaning of those
Laws, contained in the Sacred Word of God. We read but little of other Laws,
during the times of the Judges of Israel; I do believe that the multitude of
Laws did originally spring, from the iniquity of the Lawyers, and from the
iniquity of the People, scarce any words were sufficient, so to express the
truth, but either the Judge, or the Lawyer or the People, would break through
the Law; I believe there is just cause of sorrow, and of shame, to consider it.

The best way (that I know) to reform this, is to keep closest to the true
Original, which is the most true, perfect, and clear rule, and is the rule of
all rules; because all other rules, are but derivatives from thence.

Doubtless our Laws ought to be as few as may be, and those Laws distributed
into such several places, where the People dwell, such as do concern those
People, in those parts, for the Peoples ease, and comfort.

Secondly, the Laws ought to be in our own language, so as the People may
read, and observe them; because God does afford that benefit to the People, in
the giving, and publishing his Laws, which are of the most excellency. And if
we consider the end why Judges were multiplied, as Gods glory, was the chief,
so likewise the Peoples ease, and comfort is expressed: so ought it to be in
those Laws that are branches of Gods Laws, as Gods glory is the highest, and
true end of them, so likewise the Peoples ease and comfort, by, and from them,
is to be respected. A great help, both for Gods glory, and for the Peoples
comfort, is to have good, and faithful Judges; for such will not (so much)
seek themselves, (which is truly to destroy themselves) as they will seek
Gods glory, and the Peoples good. These things have bin mightily perverted, yet
God has not left us without hope, but that God will restore Judges as at the
first, and counselors, as at the beginning, then shall we be called a City of
righteousness, a faithful City.

What ever I have written in this little Book or Treatise; I do and have
only propounded to the consideration of all you that do love, honor, and fear
the true and ever living God, who is blessed for ever. I do humbly (with all
due respect to the godly and to the learned) acknowledge, I am but a weak
frail man, (of my self) I may err; therefore if any man can, and will show we
any error (provided that they bring the authority of Gods Sacred Word according
to the plain and sincere meaning of the blessed Spirit of God) I hope, God will
give me a heart, willingly (not constrainedly) to acknowledge any error; I ever
held it as a principle, that we cannot please God better, (nor bring more true
honor, and safety, to our selves) then by hunble unfeigned and willing
acknowledgement of any of our errors, in some proportion suitable to our
offenses. Receive nothing from me, further then you find it agreeable to
Scripture. But this I say, that in what ever I have here in this Book written,
I have set God always in my sight, I knowing that I am ever in his sight, to
whom I must give account for what I have written. I account it to be a matter
of no small moment to write any Book, neither had I written, if I had not
believed God called me to it, (of my self I can do no good matter) but this J
do believe that in this writing contained in this Book, I am strengthened,
protected and guided by the good and blessed Spirit of the true and ever-living
God, To whom I desire to acknowledge and give, as is Gods due, and my duty, all
praise, and service, glory, and honor, and power, because God is worthy of it,
for he has created all things, and for his Wills sake, they are, and have bin
created. Rev. 4.11.

Now beloved, and approved Commanders, and Soldiers, you that have bin helpers
of the Lord against the mighty, although I have not made mention of your Names
in this little Treatise, yet you are in my eye as men of precious esteem, and
so I believe you are in Gods account precious, (I mean such as out of godl^
zeal, and true love have acted in these Wars, of which sort I b^l^eve) there
are many amongst your Army) may I not account you amongst David's worthies? yes,
I believe, I may: and further, I believe, I may truly say that many of you,
Revel. 21.27. Are written in the Lambs book of life, and that you. Ver. 24.
Are of the people that shall be saved and walk in the light of it. Ver. 1.
That new Heaven, Ver. ^. That holy City, that new Jerusalem, God himself shall
be your God with you. Verse. 4. And God shall wipe away all tears from your
eyes, and there shall be no more death^, for the first things are passed. Cha
22.12. And behold I come shortly, says God, and my reward is with me, to give
to every man, as his works shall be. Ver. 14. Blessed are they that do his
Commandments, that their right may be in the Tre^ of life. Ver. 11. He that is
righteous let him be righteous still, and he that is holy, let him be holy
still.

Have you been co-acters in fighting Gods battles? and should I or my
Posterity, be forgetful, that you, many of you, have borne a means, that we
enjoy Gods Word freely preached, and that we still enjoy Gods sacred Word in
our own Language, and that we are not forced to bow down to dumb Idols, to
Idolatry, and that we are not cast into those dark, miserable, noisome,
golgotha's, those places which have bin the destruction of thousands, where no
eye could see, or speak to them, to pity them, where they have bin murdered
out of the view of men; I mean those accursed inquisition Houses. This comfort
only they had (which those workers of iniquity could not take from them) that
there was one open place, where the bright and beautiful eye (like to the eye
of the Morning when the glorious and brightest Sun appears) the eye of the
blessed God, and their Maker, looked clearly upon them, and vouchsafed to some
of those poor prisoners of hope, to look upon him also; have not you godly
Soldiers, bin a means, to redeem us the people of England (had we grace to see
it, to acknowledge, and be thankful for it) from that Egyptian bondage, a
corrupt form of government, wherein we like Lands, Beasts, and Asses, were
left as inheritance, from the Father to the, supposed, Sons, the Father of
one Religion, the Son of another, did they not run, and ride, with fury, and
all possible speed (horse and man) from generation to Generation to seize upon
us, thus entering in at Windows, back-doores, and in By-pathes, they (too
often) proved, in^ sheep clothing, and the blessed Spirit of God was not
given unto them, and they kept the People from true Shepherds, men of Gods
sending, upon whom the good and blessed Spirit of God would have rested.

I should much admire, that all men should not joyfully see, and acknowledge so
great deliverance, and salvation; were it not that I consider Gods righteous
judgments for sin, and also considering how prevalent custom is, insomuch
that often times it consumes truth and yet is lean still, are not your
Carriers horses often very sore loaded? and yet being accustomed to bear
burdens, they are even contented, or look no higher, they keep jogging on,
loath to go out of their pace, nor out of their accustomed way, although it
sometimes be up to their bellies in mire, and dirt, where because of times
quick motion, I must leave them to their content, and I and my house will (by
Gods gracious assistance) freely, joyfully, and with all hearty praise bless
the God of our protection, salvation, and deliverance, for our freedom, and
better way.

Have you, dearly beloved, godly Soldiers, bin used by God, as instruments,
to accomplish the precious promises of God, (recorded, concerning Babels fall,
corrupt government, and governors) and should I forget you? No verily, for I
believe that the generations to come shall have cause to bless God for you,
and your memory shall be blessed; times quick motion, bids me (unwillingly) to
forbear, and because (I conceive) I shall never more in this World speak of
you, or to you, in this kind, till I believe, we shall very shortly meet
(though of our selves unworthy, yet through the free and abundant mercy of God,
in Christ,) with joyful hearts, before God and his blessed Angels, with whom,
we shall be, and never more be separated to eternity: this span of time
hasteneth, and shorteneth, our glass runs apace, as swiftly as the Sun runs
round the World; when our work is done, come Lord Jesus, come graciously, and
quickly. Therefore I shall at present conclude my speech to you, Revel. 12.10.
(being sorry that I have not opportunity to see the faces of many of you, and
to rejoice with you for all the great works God (by you^ hands.) Numb. 23.23.
According to this time, it shall be said, of Jacob, and Israel, what has the
Lord wrought?) Then I heard a loud voice, saying, now is salvation, and
strength, the Kingdom of our God, and the power of his Christ, for the accuser
of our Brethren is cast down. Ver. 11. But they overcame him by the blood of
that Lamb, and by the word of their testimony, and they loved not their lives
unto the death. Verse. 12. Therefore rejoice ye Heavens, and ye that dwell in
them.

And now beloved Countrymen, let me speak a word to you, may I not say (to
many of you) with Jeremy, O that mine eyes were a Fountain of tears, that I
might weep day and night for the iniquity of the People? is it possible, that
after such clear, evident, and wonderful gracious works, and actings, of our
good God, (in these very times) that any rational man should be so far led
aside and prejudiced, that he should not acknowledge, with joy, and
thankfulness, to God, and to those that God has used as instruments of so
great deliverance? it is possible, for some they cry out, Oh the King, the King
is gone, (is so great pomp and riches, come to desolation, in one hour)?
others, they would have all opinions (openly manifested) to be tolerated under
pretense of liberty of conscience; others would have their own opinions, and
no other to be tolerated, that they may lord it over their weak Brethren.
Others they speak with a double heart as David took notice, and so make ready
their arrows, and bend their bows, that they may shoot at all that are
upright in heart, Psalm. 11. For they speak against Government, and Governors,
saying they hate these opinionists, they by this means, show (too evidently by
their fruits) that this is but a cloak for their own sins, for under
pretext of conformity, they shoot at Government, and governors, and in truth
at those that are the humble, true and faithful servants of our God, at all
such as are circumspect, and fear to offend God.

I would first say to them that unfeignedly desire to do Gods Will, though in
some matters, some having larger talents then others, there be difference in
their judgments, (although in many matters the difference being thoroughly, and
truly considered, is more in show then in real substance): would you take the
best and safest way? Then begin in the right manner, and place, labor to
strengthen, and encourage this present government, who, I believe, many of
them, do humbly, cordially and unfeinedly desire to do Gods good Will; now
stand still, and see the salvation of God, proceed regularly, pray earnestly
to God for them, that the good Spirit of his grace may lead them into all
truth, for doubtless, in their peace your peace and prosperity in a great
measure is contained. Let government be thoroughly settled, according to Gods
own ways which (if we pray earnestly, and walk humbly with our God) I
believe God will direct them to establish government, according to Gods mind;
you would have this issued, namely what liberty shall be granted to several,
or to all opinions, which is a matter unpossible to be done, for much must be
left to the judgment of authority, (it cannot be avoided) because many
opinions do not yet appear, and the Governors do not know their own hearts,
before hand, I know this by well observed experience, and could instance in
many cases, but I forbear. Therefore join unanimously in this, to seek, and
to pray God so to direct our present governors, that they may be so directed by
God, that they may discern, and follow that way, for the calling of our Judges
into their places, that God has prescribed, owned and blessed; for this is the
root, from whence our greatest safety, under God, consists. Such Governors,
sent of God, I know God will bless with his holy Spirit; and agree upon what
you will before hand, it will be of little moment, because it is not agreeable
to Gods proceedings: and if governors enter in at the windows, and in
by-pathes, expect bitter fruits; GOD has not promised his holy spirit to such;
let the experience recorded in Scripture, the sure rule of truth, teach us
this, such corrupted governors will be what they truly are, and they will
alter, break through, and evade Gods Laws, much more your agreements. Observe
we therefore GODS Presidents, and Rules, cleave fast, and close to GOD; now
observe GOD did first settle government, a chief Judge, before he prescribed
Rules for Judges or People; Moses was chosen before the Law was given, to
direct both him and the People; therefore do not in the mean time break out
preposterously.

And now to all discontents, whether through weakness, or malice, consider,
you did run well, you were co-actors in the late Wars, what hinders you? you
complain of Taxations, and at the same instant, by your irregularities and
gaine-sayings, do not you unavoidably pull these charges, (in a great measure)
both upon your selves, and upon us? might not matters be quieted sooner and
with less charge, did not you so crookedly imagine evil matters? you
complain of this government, in many things, both unjustly and unworthily; but
I am sure, we that seek after peace, have true cause to complain of you, for
these matters, consider, will not the issue prove bitter, and dangerous to your
selves? bear the burdens the more willingly, because they are the fruits of
sin; our governors doubtless they study, how to ease, and help you, and us,
and shall we be so ungrateful to study evil against them? Consider I pray you
that God has divolved, and turned the government, let us not strive against
God, we see it is not an arm of flesh: it must not be, that because you think
that is good to have government so, and I think it is better thus, and a third
he conceives contrary to us both: in all these cases it must not, it ought not
to be, what any of us think meet, further then what Gods counsel has
determined; which (I believe) God will guide this present government, whose
charge, and place it is, to drect our course, and this I believe, that their
hearts, and ears, are free, and open, to hear any regular, and loving
counsel; for David says he would hear the advice of his servant.

Dearly beloved Countrymen, I pray you study to be quiet, we have had
experience of the sad events of war, I do believe that if we have not profited,
it is because God has yet greater afflictions to bring upon us; labor to pray
for, to uphold, and to encourage this present government, and our selves to
walk evenly, and humbly with God, and I dare affirm it is the nearest, the
safest way, and best pleasing to God, and the most for our own comfort; how
ever I am much greived for many, especially for those malevolent inventers of
evil things, because they provoke wrath against themselves.

Now dearly beloved Fathers, the truly virtuous Generals the Lord general
Fairfax, and the Lord Lieutenant general Cromwell, who though I never saw
either of them, yet I know them by their godly and gracious actings, for the
glory of God, and for the good of us the people of England and for the good of
our posterity, cannot but unfeignedly love them, how has God used them as
instruments to free us from that miserable bondage? to them therefore and to
the rest of those worthy and godly men, that now govern this Land, may not that
which is recorded, be spoken of you all, Numb. 24.5. How goodly are thy Tents O
Jacob, and thine habitations Oh Israel? as the Valleys are they stretched
forth, as Gardens by the River side, as the Aloe Trees which the Lord has
planted, as the Cedars beside the waters. Ver. 8. God brought him out of
Egypt, his strength shall be as an Unicorn, he shall eat the Nations, his
enemies, and bruise their bones, and shoot them through with his arrows. Ver.
9. He coucheth and lies down as a young Lion, and as a Lion, who shall stir
him up, blessed be he that blesses thee, and cursed be he that curses thee.

Dearly, and unfeinedly, beloved Fathers, suffer me to use a word of
exhortation, (Moses often repeateth the same things, knowing how weak and
frail our nature is, and how apt we are to forget those most perfect and
blessed directions of our good God) consider I pray you, that as our God is a
God abundant in mercy, rich in mercy; so also he has made known himself to be
a God, jealous of his glory, and will not give his glory to another. Exodus
20.5. For I am the Lord thy God, a jealous God. Exodus 34.14. Because the Lord
whose Name is jealous, is a jealous God. Deuteronomy. 4.23. Take heed unto your
selves, least you forget the Covenant of the Lord your God. Ver. 24. For the
Lord thy God is a consuming fire, and a jealous God. Chap. 6.9. Jos. 24.19.
Joshua said, he is an holy God, he is a jealous God, he will not pardon your
iniquity, nor your sins, if you forsake the Lord. Ver. 24. And the People
said unto Joshua the Lord our God will we serve, and his voice will we obey. 1
King. 19.10. Eze. 39.25. Rev. 1.13. In the midst of the seven golden
Candlesticks, one like unto the Son of Man, clothed with a garment down to
the feet, and girded about the paps with a golden girdle. Ver. 14. His head
and hairs were white as white Wool, and as Snow, and his eyes were as a flame
of fire. Revel. 2.1. These things says he that walks in the midst of the
seven golden Candlesticks. Ver. 5. Remember thereofre from whence thou art
fallen, and do thy first works. Rev. 22.12. Behold I come shortly and my reward
is with me. Ver. 3. J am Alpha and Omega, the beginning and the end. Ver. 14.
Blessed are they that do his Commandments.

Remember that God is jealous of his honor, who says expressly we shall not
do that which seems good in our own eyes, but all that God commands. Note
this Rule well, it is Gods own Word, and counsel, the neglecting this Rule is
(and has been) the root and branches of a world of mischief. Eye the Word of
God thoroughly, follow those blessed rules prescribed by God, in the first, and
purest times, This is your wisdom and safety: no doubt, when Israel chose
Abimeleck, it seemed good in their own eyes, when they chose to be governed by
Kings, it seemed good to them when the people lived without any government,
that condition seemed good in their own eyes, although it brought the fierce
wrath of God upon them, when they worshipped the Host of Heaven, when they
worshipped Jdols and other wickedness, no doubt these matters did seem good
in their own eyes; Therefore dearly beloved lean not to your own wisdom, to
your own strength, follow the straight rules of Gods sacred Word, in the
purest manner and times, the most plainly described, consider that government
is of very weighty concernment, proceed warily with all diligence in the
form, and in the persons for that Babylon, that great City of corruptions is
compacted in, and by disorder corrupt governors and government is the very root
of all her abominations; And note it well, when Gods Church shall become a City
of righteousness, a faithful City, God names this as the principal
ingredient and cause, namely, that they shall have Judges as at the first, and
counselors as at the beginning. Observe well that frame of that Heavenly
Jerusalem, Rev. 21.2. The holy City, the new Jerusalem, Come down from God out
of Heaven, as a bride trimmed for her husband; Note well in what a beautiful
and perfect order she is proportioned, read the Chapter, see there what
blessings came to the People, when good Order comes. Ver. 4. Then God shall
wipe away all tears from their eyes, and there shall be no more death, neither
sorrow. Ver. 5. And he that sat upon the Throne said, etc. write, Ver. 6. It
is done, I am Alpha, and Omega, etc. Ver 11. Having the glory of God; and her
shining was like unto a stone, most precious, etc.

Note I pray you, what a direct opposition there is between the Babylon of
confusion, and this City ruled, and proportioned by the Wisdom of God; you
know that Babells Tower brought confusion at the first building, and from that
day to this, that great strumpet is corrupted, and defiled, by forsaking Gods
blessed Rules recorded, she slighted Gods Wisdom, she would not follow his
Prescriptions, but turned from God, and followed her own inventions. Therefore
she not being trimmed as a Bride prepared for such a glorious God, he being
jealous of his glory, does give her a Bill of divorce, for her adultery: let
this serve for to warn us to follow Gods Prescriptions, his Rules and
Presidents recorded in the Word of truth.

Note it well the maine end of the Creation of Heaven, Earth, Man and the rest
of the Creatures, was, and is, that man may learn to see the difference
between Gods good government, and evil governments; between Gods Wisdom
contained in the sacred Rules of Gods holy Word, and between man's seeming
better inventions, contrived by man's own wisdom.

Is not this the lesson that God teaches us from our cradle to ur deat?
Observe well, God lets us see the difference between his Government recorded
and prescribed in his Word of Truth, and between the Devils Government, who is
the Father of lies. Amongst the Nations of the World, God suffers evil
Governments and Governors; It is not because he wants wisdom, power,
opportunity, or goodness to reform such, but God teaches man to see the
benefit and excellency of good Governors and Government, by letting them see
evil and corrupt Governors: We have a long and large experience, from Samuel
and from Moses to this day, recorded for our instruction; I pray God that we
may now at length learn to profit, and to set a high value and price upon good
Government; proceed exactly, let no Governor enter into his place, but purely
through the door of Gods Word, follow those Rules most purely and plainly
prescribed by God himself.

Consider what is the main, the very end of Gods actings, and man's actings, all
our prosperity, our sufferngs, all our afflictions; is not this the very moving
cause, and the highest end? To teach us, that it is safest, and most for our
comfort, that we should follow those Rules prescribed by God, without turning
aside to any hand, or upon any pretense, and especially in this weighty matter
of Governors and Government; God looks upon this with a wary and with a
jealous eye, he knowing of what near concernment it is, for his glory, and man's
good; Therefore when the people went about but to alter the form of government
by himself prescribed, in what high contempt does God take this? He says, That
the people had cast God away from governing and reigning over them, in so doing.

Consider, do but take away two things, namely good Governors, and Gods good
Rules of direction, contained in his sacred Word, and this world, the people in
it, would be turned into a confused Chaos, a heap of rubbish, of ruinous
desolations, much worse then that Chaos recorded Genesis 1. When in the beginning
the Earth was void, and without form, and in darkness. Witness diverse Nations
that at this day have not Gods Laws, his blessed Word to govern them, but have
evil Governors; in such places it is certain and true, they do degenerate so
much from goodness, that the strongest captivateth and oppresses the weaker,
and they do devour one another, yea, they sell men's flesh, and women's, and
childrens flesh, as we do buy and sell beef in the shambles. Dearly beloved, we
are the very same by nature, were it not that we submit to the Government of a
good and blessed God, and to his Laws, and to his blessed Rules. Therefore now
I pray you to set a high price upon Government, good Government, for God loves
to bestow the richest and choycest mercies upon those that value them according
to their true worth; he will not prostitute such rich jewels, such precious
favors, unto such a people as make light account of them, for swine will
trample upon pearls of the greatest value; but God gives Grace to the humble,
and to the thirsty: by the hungry food is thankfully and gladly accepted, but
the full loatheth the honey comb; Israel was wanton, they slighted Gods form of
