Government, and those good Governors that were the most immediately appointed
by God himself; therefore God makes them to see the difference, he makes them
servants to serve strangers in a strange Land, in hunger, and cold, and
nakedness, and oppressed, and in the want of all things; the Lord reach us
instruction.

Therefore now, dearly beloved Fathers, join all your hearts, and endeavors
together for Gods glory, set aside, cast behind you, all comberances, all
by-respects, tread under your feet these sublunary matters, in comparison of
Gods glory, the good of your Nation, the good of your selves, and of your (and
our) posterity: consider that Satan tempted our blessed Savior with the
seeming show of these, empty, deceiptefull, deadly, lying Serpents, namely
making a show of that to be found in worldly honors, and preferments, which is
not to be found in them, if Satan labored with Christ (much more with his
Disciples) to persuade that these earthly things are more worth then Gods
favor; for the show of these, which were not his to give, labored to draw
Christ from God; Therefore (in comparison) cast behind you, under your feet,
these venomous Cockatrices Eggs of worldly honors, let them not be preferred
before Gods commands. For these deceiptfull shows of these momentany vanities,
do deceitfully work too much upon our affections, to lead us aside (out of
that good way that leads to true blessedness) into that broad path that many
great and wordly rich men do walk in, which leads to certain Destruction.

I believe, amongst you that now govern this Commonwealth, there are of Gods
precious servants, that do truly, and unfeignedly endeavor, and desire to do
Gods Will; well then, here is a precious opportunity, for if you should study
all your life, to do an act well pleasing to God, this is the very act (being
an act concerning these worldly matters) that is acceptable to God; namely, to
follow Gods choicest Rules of direction, (with all your heart, with all
diligence) in the matter of the form of government, and the persons to be
governors, that so Gods blessed Spirit may rest upon them.

For consider that if you mistake, or turn aside from Gods Commandments, and
so do mistake in the form, and persons, we are undone, the glory and splendour
of your labors are lost, for if the person of our chief Governor be not
chosen exactly, according to the choicest Rules, gathered out of the blessed,
and good Word of our God, how shall we, the People, lie down and rest in
peace, without trouble, and fear? for we know that in by-pathes Wolves and
Foxes do come into the Sheepfold, which although they should come softly to us,
as if they meant us no hurt, yet our hearts cannot be quiet, for Wolves, and
Foxes, mean us no good. Nay further, if they should come disguised in sheeps
clothing, so that we know them not by outward appearance, yet if any should
come in by any indirect means (which God forbid) in those paths those beasts of
prey come in, certainly our hearts cannot be securely and contentedly quiet,
because we shall look back upon former experiences, recorded in the Scriptures,
where we may find, that such men as have attained to the places of chief
Governors, not in a way of God, upon such persons God has not bestowed his
good (but an evil) spirit; and such persons have proved to draw the people to
sin, and have been a means to bring the fierce wrath of God upon the people.
Therefore I do seriously confess (in the presence of our glorious God) that
when I do consider the great danger, weight and charge of a chief Governors
place, I see no cause (in any worldly respect that is truly real and
substantial) why any man should covet, desire, or thirst after it: but
contrarily, considering the great charge of souls, the great account they must
give to God; for to whom much, many Talents are given, of them much shall be
required; God is a jealous God of his honor: Considering likewise the shortness
of our lives, being but even (comparatively) a moment; and considering likewise
the danger that attends men in eminent places, they are set in slippery
places; and considering likewise what diligence God requires, and self-denial,
in such places, To me it plainly appears, That a quiet or peaceably life
(with competency) is much to be preferred, and is truly and solidly better, for
a man's own comfort.

Moses and Gideon are recorded in Gods Records for their humility and wisdom,
and for that they looked upon places of charge. Governors places, as being very
weighty to bear, above their own abilities. Consider therefore, that if any man
should attain Government in any bypath, not being sent of God, into what a
deep, miserable, and woeful case (for soul and body) should such plunge
themselves and so many thousands of Souls? for this undoubtedly I shall
expect, that where any do attain governors places, not according to Gods
Rules, that to such God will not give his good Spirit, but rather an evil, and
a deceiving Spirit. Note I pray you, that although God was offended with the
People, yet because the People, followed Gods counsel, in accepting the person
that God saw meet to Govern them, therefore the Spirit of God came upon Saul,
all the time that he rightfully reigned; but presently when God had rejected
him from governing, it is noted, and recorded, that an evil spirit came upon
him, though he retained his place after. Therefore I humbly request you, lay
aside all worldly respects, in this case, and join all your strength,
diligence, and hearts, cheerfully and unanimously for Gods glory and the good
of us your People, and of our (and of your) posterity.

Remember, dearly beloved, how often God does repeat these instructions,
namely, that his People should diligently take heed, to observe) and note his
Commandments, (and meditate in them, day and night, to do and to observe
them; how often does God admonish them to take heed, not to add, nor diminish,
to or from his Commandments? and not to turn aside to the right nor left
hand? how many eminent examples has God recorded of his anger, against such as
have cast away his Commandments? and likewise his blessing upon them, that
with the greatest intention, have followed those ways that God directed; and
our Savior tells us that those that do Gods Commandments, are like to the
wise builder, that builded upon a Rock. Consider what great compassion God
has showed to us that are Gentiles by nature, and were Aliens from the Israel
of God; and Strangers from the Covenant of the Promises; now God has broken
down that partition wall, and has given us hope of salvation, and has made
us partakers of those precious promises of Grace, that are like to the balm of
Gilead; God through his blessed Son, and our Savior, has freely forgiven us
our Offenses; and has given unto us an assured hope of salvation; Remember
then what Christ says, that if we love him, we should keep his
Commandments. And consider, we shall get no benefit, by turning from our God,
if we could obtain the wings of the Morning, and go over the face of the whole
Earth, yet we sall certainly find, that there is no God, like to our God, nor
no devices, or inventions of Men, to be compared with those most beautiful,
and perfect ways of our God. And notwithstanding that Israel knew all this,
yet how apt were they, and how often did they forsake the strong and gracious
God, and rejected his Commandments; And preferred their own inventions,
before Gods Commandments, and before his Blessed Institutions; in so much that
GOD complained, that the Ox acknowledge^ his owner, and the Ass his Masters
Cribbe, but Israel would not obey the Lord, their God.

Consider what could God have spoken, or done more unto us, he has sent his
Prophets rising up early, he has set before us Life and Death, Good and
Evil, Prosperity and Adversity, God has set before us an eternal weight of
glory, a Crown of glory, God has given us, (us unworthy such great and
precious favors) hope, nay sure hope, that we shall shortly (our glass runs
apace) see God and enjoy him (and the company of his blessed Saints and
Angels) to all eternity, who is the Fountain, and perfection of all good,
beyond what the eye has seen, or the ear heard, and beyond what ever entered
into the heart of man to conceive.

Consider I pray you, that notwithstanding that Israel knew many of these
things, yet they forsook the Fountain of living waters, in so much that God
says of them, Esai. 48.18. Oh that thou had hearkened to my Commandments,
then had thy prosperity been as the Flood, and thy righteousness as the Waves
of the Sea, thy seed also had been as the Sand, that is numerous: and our
blessed Savior says, Mat. 23.27. O Jerusalem, Jerusalem, which killest the
Prophets, and stonest them that are sent unto thee, how often would I have
gathered thy Children together, as the Hen gathers her chickens, under her
wings, and you would not; Ver. 38. Therefore behold your habitation shall be
left unto you desolate.

But (Dearly beloved Fathers) I hope better things of you. God has used you
already as instruments of his glory to do great things; God has by you opened
such a door for Reformation, as (I believe) has not been since the days of
Samuel the Prophet. Now you have a precious Pearl^ in your hands, now you have
an opportunity, the Lord give you hearts not to slight it, but to improve it,
for the honor of God, and for the good of his Church and People; you may (I
believe, if God give you hearts) be a means, that we may have Judges as at
the first, and Counselors as at the beginning, then shall we be called a City
of righteousness, and a faithful City. Isa. 1.16. And then shall Peace and
Truth meet together, as Moses m^t Aaron in the Mount of God, and they kissed
each other, Exodus 4.27.

And then shall we be a People whose governors, and government shall be (like
in form) like unto the resemblance of that blessed form, and frame of
government, in Heavenly places, amongst the blessed Saints and Angels; which
they do, (and the Elect children of God shall) enjoy to all Eternity.

The consideration of that blessed, and happy Government in Heaven drew me to
desire, that our Government upon Earth, might be (in some proportion) like to
it; this was the first mover, (under G d) that caused me to write these few
Lines, and it is the utmost (and only) end of My Endeavors.

FINIS.
Imprimatur,

John Downame.
December. 28. 1649.
